ordinate course heauens sterres aswell fixed also planettes mouable heuens placed sundry disposicions whose dyuers operacions earthe bringeth foorth hir fruites kyndes due season whiche fyrst growe ripenesse foloweth decaie thynges varie accordynge tyme nowe pleasaunt sommer thanne wythered wynter nowe plenty full aboundance thynges tyme baraine scarcitie c reason also affirmeth muche wyse philosophiers put generation one thyng corrupcion nothynge maie longe endure one state either encreaseth empeired learnyng haue authoritees manifold emonge others salomon saieth thynges haue tyme saieth tyme peace tyme warre tyme mery time sadde experience also manifest doth take tyme tyme accordyng therto tempre dispose conueigh procedynges shall noo brynge theim effecte prosperous successe thanne songe shalbe allowed wherof syngers kepe theyr true tyme dooe runne awaie therewith makyng ouermuche haste dragge comyng slowly mutabilitie tyme variable passeth awaie swiftely length suche violence olde poetes willing descriue ti e liuely according veraie propretie therof dooe sette foorth figure man hauing wynges wherwith fligh hauing also great sithe handes mowe cut downe thinges appoynted season deuoureth consumeth thynges long processe euen manifesteth thynges neuer hydden secrete wherefore veritie called doughter tyme hath also sister called occasion saied sage poetes vnder whose woordes vnder vaile hidden many depe misteries wyllynge descriue dooe feigne haue wynges hir fete declare therby swift passyng awaie also feigne hir haue hir heare growing hanging long downe forpart hir hedde hynder part smothe bare alde signifiyng therby cometh towarde man may take sure holde hir hir longe heares case mysse take holde suffryng hir passe hym holde taken hir behynde runneth awaie without recouerie also iuigned vnto hir compaignion called repentance whiche nothyng lyght foote occasion hir escape man leaueth behynde hir kepe hym compaignie whereby ment occasion taken whan offereth hir selfe manne partie refuseth hir offre shall ceasse duryng lyfe forthynke folie suffryng hir departure wherfore sen apparent obeiyng tyme necessary wha behold manifold iniuries doen maiestee subiectes realme vnnaturall vnkind enemy sundry party diuerse many way whiche ye haue longe suffred neuerthelesse dayly renewed manifest euident youre hyghnesse dryuen geat swoorde whyche force deteyned power reuenge wronges wroughte malice vntruthe onelesse ye shoulde thought regarde honour due imperiall maiestie high prince salomon booke entitled ecclesiastes vpon foorth mennes eies noble actes thereby stiere enkendle hertes myndes beholder doeth muche reioyce beholdyng hercules peinted walle cl thed lyon skynne mighty hande spoyled drawynge hym cerberus hell hounde iii hydous heddes whome brought dominion pluto doeth reioyce heare conquest golden fliece iason isle colchos thus appereth doen vertuousely enbrace honourable trauaile deserue haue immortall fame emong whiche moste victorious conquerours although moste excellent maiestee maie without controuersie doubte worthily chalenge take chief place yet would maiesties owne face offre selfe setter thereof oncles expresse veritee grace procedynges dyd manifestly publysshe declare maie possybly encurre maner suspicion flatterie adulation comparyng noble dedes forenamed great princis vnto moste woorthy actes shall appere manifest anniball helpe frenchemen passed mountaines italie fought three fower notable battailes great ruine romaine achieued rather crafty sleightes policy strength theim whose helpe valiantnesse conduite preuailed carthaginenses subdued kyng sypbax thynges seemed men notable emong others chief authour titus liuius auaunce renoume wrote thereof noble goodly historie moste lucky victory hyghnes hath late agaynst promisse breaker double dealynge scottes furthermore partely breuitie partely thyng beeyng lately dooen neither bruite memory therof freshe much superfluous recite haue thought best wholly omitte long recitall late noble politike myghty conquest bollayne neuer heretofore prince subdued scarcely approched vnto lefte thynge inuin ible therefore conquestes compare moste famous subduynge romayne monster hydra whose heddes wer many lest theim pestylent thought could neuer without great assistence diuine power haue subdued heddes moste folowynge warre vppon vacceis whiche warres brought passe ended retourned farre ryuer tagus banysshed people countreys aforesayde assembled togyther reysed carpetanes whose helpe numbre hundred thousande trustyng theyr great multitude came newly vpon carthaginenses anniball perceyuing great power commyng vpon hym absteyned batayle priuily nyght conueyed ouer fourde thense withdrue people good space enemy myght haue place come ouer ryuer set xl elephantes alonge ryuer syde myght redy oppresse entryng water also co maunded horseman soone footemen entred water shulde fiersly assayle carpetanes vacceis carteians thynkyng theyr ennemies feare fledde theym intendynge pursue without foresyght order spede makyng great clamour euery man rashely toke next way water hannibal horsmen perceyuing entred fourde violently ranne litell peyne ouerthrewe great number fotemen water whiche thyng easy doo footeman strength streame coulde wyse susteyne force horseman onely rushe horse though ryder vnarmed able ouerthrowe foteman feble stay fote water thus drowned passed ouer ryuer oppressed elephantes shorte space vtterly discomfyted ouercome whiche last entred ryuer though escaped danger horseman coulde recule backe agayn tolande assemble togyther set selfe aray annibal freshe band men entred water quyckly folowed chased fewe escaped whervpon shortly conquered al carpetanes reste tyll theyr capitayne healed durynge whiche time rest battayle citizen vnoccupied fortified selfe strongly perceyued assautes come shulde fierce perillous whan hanniball cured wounde siege warre became deadly terrible carthaginens dayly increased noumber cl theyr engins bet downe walles sagunt ground dyuers partes semed sundry tymes haue citie within walles lacked strengthe men defended thus determined moue anniball alcon saguntine brought annibal shewed vnto hym shulde intended haue peace whiche condition peace semed vnto alcon vnreasonable wherfore thinkyng saguntines wold case agree vnto remained styll wolde retourne agayne citie affirmynge worthy dye vnder couenates wold treate peace whan alcon denied saguntines wold receyue suchetruce alorcus aforesayd beinge souldiour annibals ennemies brought pretor saguntine senate whan multitude common lytell withdrawen thus beganne oration p citezyn messanger alcon came anniball require peace lykewise broughte hym vnto condition comyng nowe ben vayne thing done shuld nother annibals oratour fugityue haue come vnto tyme seing either owne defaute el tarieth ennemies lest shulde ignorant certayne condition offered bothe peace safegard olde frendshyp hospitalitie hath ben betwene v come fyrst wolde ye shulde perswade selues welth none cause speake wordes wyl declare may well perceyue longe able owne power make resistence trusted haue succour romayns neuer made mention peace nowe seing hope succour romains stregth walles fayle vnable longer resist bring peace necessary ryghtuous iuste peace yet hope yf anniball beinge conquerour doth sende people subdued wyll receyue must consyder beinge conquered muste conquerour receiue whiche goodnes wyl giue reward condition peace wyl take citie whyche hath broken parte almoste wonne wyll leaue fieldes also assigne place shall buylde newe citie commaundeth also golde syluer goodes publike priuate brought hym contented suffer selues wyues child passe safe garde ye go citie romayns capytayn agaynst hym scipio passed ouer padus remoued campe ryuer called ticinus wold gyue battayle exhorte encourage men began oration vnto p louyng souldiours armye fraunce wolde speake vnto intende present tyme say shuld nede stere incourage horseman whyche ryuer rhodanus soo valyantly ouerthrewe theyr ennemies legion folowed fugitiue ennemye nowe bycause hoste sent senate rome spayne make warre vnder brother cneius scipio intent shulde haue bothe consull capitayne agaynste anniball carthaginenses wyllyngly toke vpon warre newe capitayn new souldiours shuld vse fewe wordes notwithstandyng lest ye shulde ignorant kind warre knowe whome ye shall fyght ye shall vnderstand ye shall haue laste warres ye subdued bothe lande sea ye toke truage perforce space twenty yeres also wonne sardinia sicilia prey warre therfore battayle ye must haue harte myndes wont conquerours ennemies muste nedes suche harte happen men ouercome gyue batayle theyr owne hardynesse courage bicause chose onelesse thynke hauyng theyr hole army freshe lusty withdrewe durste encounter v battayle beyonde mountaynes whyche loste two partes bothe horseman footemen passynge ouer mountaynes shulde haue nowe hope trust fewe left haue loste harte strength nowe ymages yea rather shadowes men men dede beinge clonged together hunger colde feynte febled emonge rocky hylles besydes theyr synewes veynes shronke togyther colde snowe theyr membres wythered froste yse theyr harnies shaken rusty broke theyr horse feble lame enemy must fyght ye ar leuynges ennemies ennemies feare nothynge shall fyght foos shalbe thought mountayns haue fyrst ouercome taken honour v perchance necessary mete goddis without man helpe without battayle shulde ouercome truce breaker violated disceyued shulde next goddis theyr mynisters bryng vtter confusyon peraduenture many wyl suppose speake wordes proudly hyghly onely exhortation comfort shulde thynke otherwise selfe therfore ye shall vnderstand sent spayn myne owne prouince whether nowe going myne host shulde haue vsed bothe felowshyp counsayle brother peryls ieopardies shoulde haue fought rather hasdrubal lesse power hanniball shuld haue lesse withstandyng whan arriued shyppes beyonde costeo fraunce landyng hearde great bruite anniball sendyng certayne horseman pitched tentes rhodanus company ouerthrewe put flyghte theyr chaunce mete battayle bycause could footemen ouertake myne ennemy whiche fled returned shippes good spede could make sayling great compasse arriued mete hym front mountaines intent gyue hym battayle proue whether earthe hath brought forthe sodainly within space xx yeres carthaginenses wonte bredde kynd warred yles egates remembre welle sold erix xviii pece come wold also longe proue whether anniball folower hercules iourney sayth orels tributary stipendary seruaunt people rome left father haue shewe bandes truce writen hande father amilcar beinge commaunded capitayne withdrewe garrison citie erix lamentyng frowning receiued greuous lawes made agaynst carthaginenses subdued couenanted romayns depart sicilia pay tribute therfore souldiours wolde haue fyghte onely good courage ye wonte agaynste ennemies also suche indignation displesure though sawe seruantes armed fyght agaynst myght wolde whan inclosed erix hunger hardest soorest punyshement amonge men haue destroyed might allabours yf wolde haue sayled victorious n uye affrica short space battaile vtterly haue destroyed carthage pardoned theym made peace subdued toke theym protection defence whan sore greued warres affrike benefites shewed vnto folowinge furious yonge man come conquere countrey wolde god battayle nowe honour healthe safetie v fyght nowe possession sicilia sardinia whiche stro e tymes paste nowe muste fyght italy none armye behynde v wil withstande ouerthrowen nother mo mountaines ouer while passyng men might prouide newe succour must resist eue shuld fight walles rome euery man must thinke armour couereth defendeth body also wife small child let man care owne house family let likewise haue minde senate people rome beholdeth conflict battayle vppon fortune present tyme dependeth prosperitie citie hole empyre rome p example wordes anniball exhorted souldiours fight valiantly cap xi whyles scipio consulle maner exhorted romaine anniball thynkyng fyrst encourage men dedes wolde exhort theym wordes disposed army compasse beholde fyght thanne brought middes mountayne men nnde whome taken prisoner layde also place armour frenchemen whyche hadde ouercome caused one coulde speake language inquere prysoners whyche yf losed theyr bondes wold take hors armour fight theyr line whan hadde desyred armour battayle caused lotte caste accordyng lotte losed great number leapyng skypping theyr maner euery shortely toke armour beinge ioyfull glad dye honour lyue shame capti itie incontinent called souldiours aboute hym made oration maner forme folowynge p ye haue mynde remembrance example stranger fortune longe passed ye shuld haue euen nowe wayinge owne fortune chaunce haue ouercome battayle captiues wherfore ye must thynke prisoner nowe shewed shewed spectakle beholde certayn resemblance owne chaunce condition case ye nowe ouercome taken tell whether fortune hath gyuen greatter bandes vrgent necessitie hath gyuen heretofore captiues two sea doo compasse bothe ryght hande lefte shyppes haue none escape awaye withall water padus aboute v violent ryuer rhodanus backes hygh mountayns ye passed great peyn peryll wherfore louing souldiours ye must eyther ouer come ennemies fyrst encounter el slayne self fortune hath brought suche necessite nedes ye must fight die fortune shal giue rewardis ye subdue enmies mortall men desire greatter immortall goddis shuld valiantnes recouer agayne onely sicilia sardinia whiche wonne forefather might thought sufficient reward case spede wel euer romains haue goten many victory triumphes dominion nowe possesse shall princis lordes ruler wynne ryche preye fauour helpe goddis arme youre selfe sette forthe boldely ye haue hytherto longe ynoughe chacynge beastes wyde large mountaynes lusitania celtiberia founde worty praye rewarde recompence soo many peril nowe tyme get ryche prays measuryngly great rewardes accordynge desertes trauaile enterprysing great iourney passing ouer many mountayns ryuers many kyndes armed people fortune hath gyuen ende trauayle fortune wyl rewarde accordyng costes charge haue ben ye shuld suppose vyctory harde battayle great name oftentimes small host hath made great doutful battayle agaynl noble people yea kynges haue ben ouer come lytel moment take away terrible sound name rome compared great warres xx yeres manhod good fortune speake wyl remembre thynges late done ye come hyther pyllars hercules occean sea frome furthest parte worlde passyng conqueryng many fierce cruell nation spayne france shall nowe fyght yonge vntaught souldiours late beaten ouercome frenchemen yet vnknowen theyr capitayne vnto theym shall born brought vp noble hous father hath ben chastyser spayne france haue conquered onely people mountaynes also passage whiche moche compare selfe weake capytayne fourtenyght olde wandrynge frome hoste hooste yf man day wolde shewe army carthage army romains togyther tell whyche hoste gouernour banner badge surely worthy warrior esteme lyttell none whome haue done worthy feate warre tyme ye dyd extolle laude thought worthy gyftes preferrement nowe shall lyke father capytayne enter battayle agaynste people nother knoweth v theym knoweth euer caste myne eye see nothynge amonge hardynesse strength moste aunciente famous footemen mooste noble armed vnarmed horseman moste faithfull hardy carthaginenses felowes shall fyght countrey iuste ryghtuous quarell brynge warre banner dysplayed italy noysome romaynes moche boldly may fyght moche hope courage v inuade stronger theyrs onely defende besydes theyr wronge vnworthy dealyng towarde v bothe kendle encourage myndes fyrst beinge capitayne requyred destruction sagunt lykewyse requyred delyuered romayns put deathe moste cruell proude nation dothe thynges theyr owne brayne iudgement wyll determyn whome shall haue warre peace thing thynke ryghtefull wylle appoynte hylles fluddes boundes mere whyche may passe yet wyll obserue place termes whych haue sette prescribed selues thou shalt saye passe iberus lest thou make saguntines sagunt iberus therefore shall moue thyther appoynted place esteme litell haue taken v auncient prouinces sardinia sicilia woll haue spayn also wynne wyll haue affrica may well say affrica also haue sent two consul yere one affrica spayne nothynge lefte v muste fayne wynne agayne sworde feare compelle theym lyke cowardes flee v haue place ynoughe receyue theym knowe countreys wayes wherby escape behoueth play valyant men settyng six seuen eyther vanquyshe elles yf fortune frowne rather manfully dye battayle slayne fleyng away haue sayd fast fixed myndes say certayne haue ready vyctorye p howe scipio fought togither howe hurt cap xii vhan exhortation men warre bothe partes kendled stered battayle romaine pitched tentes ticinus beganne make bridge fyrst made towre vpon safegarde bridge while workyng occupied theyr worke hanniball sent maharball wynge numidies v c horseman destroye fieldes suche frendes romayns chargyng theym spare frenchemen stere princis forsake roman amitie whan bridge made scipio con eied army ouer pytched within v myles anniballes campe whan romaine hoste approched maharball called backe wh n anniball coulde neuer inough stire souldiours battayle promised gyftes rewardes ye fredome landes also affrica spayn italy theyr owne pleasure case myght obteyne vpper hande dydde sacrifice vnto goddis holding lambe lefte hande ynt stone ryght hand desyrynge iupyter goddis slea lambe yf wolde weake promyse euery receiuynge sure hope desyred battayle roman made suche haste bycause feared strange token fyghtes lyttell wolfe se e come theyr campe rent tore mette hym selfe escaped without hurte dyuers suche token straunge shewed amonge romaynes whan scipio soughte deligently myght sygnifye went certayne horseman hym lytte l hyll ere adioynyng viewe number demeanour annibals hoste chance mette anniball certayne horseman hym also ridden forthe viewe countreys aboute whan almost mette great care diligence set selfes aray fyghte battayle stronge season doubtfull whyle romain fotemen fledde backe battayle beinge myngled horseman caused great confusion whan numidian horseman whiche wynges came theym also fledde partes campe conflict consul scipio soore wounded great peyn horseman caried fielde theyr great discomforte wherfore nyght folowyng romanes makyng litell noyse myght theyr ennemies shulde haue noo knowledge remeued ticinus padus came placentia anniball wyst departed ticinus mago spanyshe fotemen swam ouer water quyckly anniball hygher parte ryuer passed ouer hoste great spede might within fewe day came pitched placentia morowe syght enemy ranged hoste sette aray redy gyue battayle nyght folowyng reason sedition arose romane army many frenchemen slayne came raide whervpon two thousand fotemen two hundred horseman frenchemen sleinge watchemen gate fledde vnto anniball whome gentilly entertained kedled hope exceding great rewardes sent euery man home owne citie therby allure tourne myndes common theyr countrey vnto hym scipio demyng slaughter token frenchemen wolde forsake hym beinge touched yuell dede madnesse fallen vppon theym wolde runne harneys withstandynge wounde greued hym soore yet pryuily myght nyghte tyme remoued hooste ryuer trebia pytched hygher place lyttell hylles ylle horseman anniball hauynge knowlege therof sente fyrste certayne numidian thanne horseman whyche shulde sicilia army iourney receiued letter senate entring carthaginenses italy requiring aide consule sone might whan perceiued layd garrison diuers place defend prouinces came selfe strong power italy kepe costes thus whan two consul met together al power rome assembled ageinst anniball withstanding one consul beinge ab ted fyrst battayle sore wounde wold rather prolong matter fight freshe lusty therfore fierce wold haue delay thinking great honour vnto might recouer agayn consul lost wherfore sayd man wold deferre battaile weaker harte body remebrance wound refrain fighte also tyme ought prolonged sicke folkes shal tary lose time third consull army shall abyde carthaginenses haue pitched theyr tentes italy weluere citie rome seeke nowe neither sicilia sardinia afore conquered spayne beyonde iberus come driue expell romaynes owne lande natiue countrey say howe moch wold father wont warre walles carthage lament sawe v child ye two consul two hostes tremblynge quakynge italie within owne campe carthaginenses wonne al feldis betwene alpes apenni u wordes spake hurt felowe pretory also chosynge offycers rome prouoked hym make haste leste taryinge felowe beyng hurte myght occasyon theyr losse preyse victory lest warre myght comytted new consul whose election hand thin ge consydered prepared batayle haste annibal although thought nothyng shalde done vnwarely sen two cosuls mette together warre shulde cruell strong yet dyd mystruste good fortune bycause fyrst battayle also busy intentiue battayle whyles thoughte souldiours ennemies yong rawe warres while one beste consull yet hole woundes while frenchemens harte armye great numbre stronge hardy whose courage thought knewe well wolde rather dyminyshe increace whan shoulde brought theyr owne countrey thynges considered sent certayn frenchman abrode cuntrey spy shewed hym romayns redy fyght anniball wente see prouide place disceyte myddes betweene two hostes fielde shuld aryuer whiche closed side greatte hygh bankes sette aboute wiedes fennes whiche almoste couered grounde yonge wyllowes shrubbes also hygh busshes thornes whyche whan serched perceyued place obscure darke ynough hyde inbusshement horseman sayde brother mago place shalt thou kepe thou shalte sayde chose vnto one thousande horseman oone thousande fotemen best myn army lye couert place whan tyme shal requyre shal shew therto appertayneth ye sure ye shall haue ennemies blynd feates warre whan mago horseman fotemen deliuered anniball commaunded numidian horseman nexte mornyng passe water trebia ryde vp downe gate ennemies campe whan hadde castyng throwyng theyr tentes station prouoked issue batail alluring pursue shuld litell litell recule backe ouer said riuer residu capitayns comaded shuld cause al men dyne refreshe selfes redynes shuld called battaile sempronius bearyng rumour numidies brought army beinge desyrous battayle ryuer whervnto reculed backe appointed anniball weather extremely colde showed fast souldiours hadde taken sustenance made prouision strength kepe theyr body warme colde frost snowe haste folowyng numidian theyr crafty ennemyes fledde theym entred ryuer nowe water rysen nyghte reason snowe high theyr brestis whan cam water theyr body stark benommed colde scarsely could holde theyr armour vpon also towarde myddes daye beganne faynt hunger meane season anniball caused great fyres made souldiours tentes euery man might warme also put oyle gloues whyche shoulde souple ioyntes membres whan hearde theyr ennemies passed ryuer beinge lusty bothe body harte euery man toke weapon went battayle anniball ordred battayles circumspectly fyrst sette forthe thrower dartes whyche yles called baleares light harneysed fotemen numbre viii footemen also bestowed ii wynges x horseman rested great strength battayle wynges also departed elephantes puttynge craftily fyght ennemies horse whyche wont strangenes syght vnaccustomed sauour scattered abrode battayle footemen maynteyned season none reason horsmen elephantes also sodayne commynge mago numidian fiersely assayled romaynes theyr backes stryken suche feare fledde partes ieoparded take water ageyne escaped theyr tentes fewe either drowned depe water el slayne theyr ennemies chase water syde many toke ryght way placentia therby saued syde carthaginenses soo beaten rayne myxte snowe intollerable colde beastes elephantes men almost peryshed ryuer trebia caused retourne pursuite roman almoste deade colde came theyr campe small ioy theyr victory next night scipio conueyed hoste ouer ryuer trebia placentia vnware carthaginenses reason vehement storme rayne felle nyght coulde remouyng elles peyne theyr woundes werynes labour dyssembled matter toke hede ther thus roman conueyed peasibly placentia then passed ouer padus cremona whan chance therof knowen rome arose suche dayn feare among though theyr ennemies ben come alredy baners displayde gate rome neyther hope succour wherby myght defende theyr enemyes gate walles one consul ouercome ticinus called frome sicilia helpe hym nowe bothe beinge togyther ouercome two hostis capitayns legion left stande p hanniball intendyng take certayn castell stelthe encountred consull wounded put worse great slaughter people wonne vicu nias howe cn scipio spayne ouerthr hanno battayle cap xiiii vvhan sempronius chaunce escaped great daunger enemy returned rome chosyng new co suls parliament cneius seruslius c flaminius created consulles whiche thinge done came placentia thynkyng passe wynter quietly place roman quiete moche winter tyme numidian hoste anniball sparkled abrode co e troubled euery syde certayn market towne castell farre placentia ryche strongly fensed thither went hannibal horseman suche lyght harneysed thynkyng wynne assa nyght watchemen perceyuing intent reised suche crye hearde placentia consull next morning horseman legion good order folowyng came thither gaue battayle whiche anniball wounded wherby carthaginenses suche feare gaue backe peace lasted whyles anniballes wounde healynge ere fully cured went place called vicunuias place surely kepte romanes great numbre garrison townes also reason assemble people countrey beyng afrayde numidian whiche roued abrode fledde thither succour people say many numbre hering noble defendyng castell adioynynge placentia thynkyng great feate great route people without order ranne rome prepared gyue battayle caathaginenses first day met roman good tune wonne victory playn fielde also draue tentes indeuored selfes wynne campe anniball setting certayn fotemen defend gate entree campe causing rest well fotemen horseman recule dyd sette aray within campe intent redines rushe vpon enemy sone made signe roman seing coulde wynne campe blewe retreite whan anniball sawe bataile slakid roman began recule back campe set forthe horseman ryght hand lefte hym selfe fotemen came campe gaue theym stronge battayle puttyng moch dysplesure anon nyght departed lyke losse slaughter bothe sydes p whyles thynges doone italy cn scipio sent spayne hoste partely force partly amitie olde frendshyp brought countreys lusitania riuer iberus vnder obedience roman also fame gentil entertayning people broughte inhabitauntes mountaynes wylde nation assured frendes redy theyr armour succour aide roman best power hanno anniball hadde left defence region knowynge actes scipio arryuall fearyng leste shuld hym put possession countreye appoynted fight hym matter ouerfar gone pytched campe farre hoste roman scipio knowyng yf long tary batayle shulde haue hym also hasdruball bothe lefte defence countrey thought better hym mete theym theyr hostes seuerally thanne matche bothe hostes togither wherfore made spede mete fyrste hanno company whyche battayle slayne vi thousand carthaginenses ii taken capytayn hanno tentes certain town also nere vnto campe called stissus hasdruball herd discom iture felowe hanno passed ryuer iberus viii fotemen one thousande horseman intendynge mete romaynes theyr fyrst commynge whanne hearde ouerthrowe hanno people tourned toward sea chance met many roman left ship far tarracon wandryng abrode vpon sea costis takynge hede theyr ennemies people mystrustynge nothynge beynge neglygent reason theyr late prosperous successe negligent person many rest drone shyppes greate feare lesse hym selfe afrayd scipio commyng urste longe tary party army passed ryuer iberus distroyed fieldes illergites bryngyng subiection p annibal passed dangerous ryuer arnus great losse meane cattall fenny yre caused hym lose one eies haste flaminius consule maketh gyue hym battayle cap xv soone sprynge yere dyd appere annibal goinge place wintred bycause sayd flamminius consule come aretium withstandyng easy better way yet bycause aboute toke nexte waye ouer greatte peryllous fennes tyme ryuer arnus hadde ouerflowed hygher tymes past commanded spanyardes affricans moste part olde souldiours stuffe go lest whan constrayned stay place theyr necessary shulde wantyng next theym set frenchemen bycause wolde haue hoste myddell lest truste last commanded horseman come giuing charge mago certayne beste numidian come behynde brynge forth army specially frenchemen lest wearynes feare long way shuld cause stay slyp away faynt fearefull people suche busynes fyrst company walowyng thycke mudde depe water skarcely sauyng selues drownyng folowed theyr standardes guydes frenchemen folowed theym coulde nother saue theym selues fallynge nother whan downe well aryse agayne nother coulde harte comfort body hope comforte harte drewe weary membres peyne theym one fell theyr harte ouercomme wearynes constrayned dye watche suffred iiii day iii nyghtes without slepe chiefe cause theyr confusyon whan could fynde dry place myght rest theyr weary body water coueryng al erth heaped theyr stuffe baggage water one packe whervpon rested saued selfes heapes dead cattell whiche dead way stede beddis many faint feble whiche eased lytel space anniball hym selfe hauynge sore eies reason intemperate sprynge tyme yere chaunged heate nowe colde caried vpon elephant remained bicause shulde hyghe water yet great watche colde reason fenny ayre beinge noysome heade bycause place tyme heale loste one eies whan passed fennes without great losse bothe men beastes soone came dry ground pytched campe hauing certayne knowlege espies romane hoste aretium cuntrey plesant fertyle italy p consull fierse cruell ioy pride newe office onely lyttell feared lawe dignitie father senate also wanted feare immortall goddis fortune also nouryshed foolyshe hardynes prosperous successe wel ciuile busynes affayres home certain foreyn batayles appered wente aboute thynges cruelly ouer hastily nother counsaylynge goddis men howe moche redye folowe owne foly moche busyer anniball prouoke stere hym wherfore leauing ennemies left hande went towarde fessula intendyng distroy fieldes hetruria shewed consull great waste destruction spoylynge frendes myght bothe robbynge slaughter burnyng thintent shulde therby rather prouoked battayle flamminius owne nature gyuen busy although ennemy wolde haue ben quiete rest whan sawe goodes frendes caryed awaye neyghbours bourned face thynkynge dishonour vnto hym see anniball wander throughe myddes italy taking pleasure without resistence determyned incontinent gyue battayle although many men perswaded hym shuld tary commynge felowe consul shulde counsayles hoostes togyther procede vnto theyr enterpryse agaynste annibal meane tyme horseman lyght harneysed footemen lette hym frome robbynge destroyinge countrey contrary aduertisement gyuen hym beinge angrye rushed forth counsel howse quikly caused baners standerdes dysplayde lepte hym selfe vpon horse incontinent hors sodainly fell cast consull earthe whyche vnlucky begynnynge caused present greatly feare successe therof p battayle trasimenus deathe consul flamminius many romayns cap xvi anniball whyle distroyed wasted cruell warre fieldes betwene citie cortona lake trasimenus thynkynge harte enemy sooner moued redresse iniuries theyr frendes came place meete treason disceyte great lake fenne trasimenus dydde almoste ioyne vnto hylles cortona place one onely strayte narowe waye enter afterwarde fieldes waxed lyttell broder larger ouer playne hylles arose great heyght fayre playne place anniball pytched campe onely affricanes spanyardes dyd reste rest lyght harneysed men army brought backe hylles disposed horseman nere mouthe narowe entre hylles myght secretly couer hide commaundyng soone roman one passed straytes horseman shuld appere theyr backes soo shoulde inclosed hemmed partes hauynge waye escape reason hylles greatte lake p flamminius folowynge ennemies come aboute settyng sonne lake next day early mornynge whan scarcely day lyght hoste passed straytes whan people began stray abrode larger felde saw al place occupied theyr enemy aper ceyued treason bothe behynde ouer theyr heades whan anniball knowyng ennemies enclosed lake hylles one syde whyche desyred also compassed army side gaue signe men sodeinly inuade ennemies commandement anon diligence executed ru nyng downe hylle assaylyng romanes partes one thyng moche amased romaynes sodayne straunge chaunge thereof arose frome brode lake myste thycker darker hylles apparence whyche letted theym syght true knowledge maner theyr ennemies inuasyon noyse sodayne affraye arose amonge theym perceyued theym selues betrayde hemmed battayle begonne bothe bothe sydes coulde put good aray take theyr armor drawe theyr swerdes p consull flamminius whan people thus oppressed feare hym selfe man great courage lyttell affrayde ordered troubled company sette order well tyme place wolde serue styll exhortyng meanes myghte abyde fyghte shewynge theym booted theym praye call theyr goddis make vowes theym theyr delyuerance nowe waye theym escape strengthe hardynesse way made swerd lesse feare dydde take lesse ieopardye perylle shoulde noyse soo greatte wordes counsaylle capitayne coulde hearde dismayde skarsely knewe theyr standerdes place repayre vnto hadde scante harte drawe theyr weapon theyr harneis rather burthen defence myght heare moche noyse clamour wounded lyttell coulde see fled fleing hapned fall company romanes fought earnestly stayed fleinge commynge towarde battayle discomfyture suche mette whyche fledde away discouraged fledde also laste whan perceyued way escape felle earnestly fyghtyng kepyng order oraray companyes happed theym falle togyther beganne battayle fyerce partes endured almoste thre howres euery cruell moste daungerous consull strengthe hoste folowed hym euer parte sawe men daunger quyckly diligently rescued beinge valiant bothe myghtyly assayled ennemies defended citezens vntyll one insubria called ducarius knowyng bothe horse face sayd company consu longe agone confounded legyons distroyed bothe cyties fieldes nowe shall sende sowle company frendes redy hath slayne hyttynge hors spurres ranne violently thyckest ennemyes route sleinge squyre whyche mette hym vnhappyly way afterwarde speare ranne consull body hadde spoyled hym stronge company romayne knyghtes withstande hym deathe beganne roman flee al partes nother hylles lake coulde lette theym wandred blynd men straites ouer rockes fallyng one ouer whan coulde fynde none waye toke next way fennes runnynge water ouer head shulders moste parte drowned awayte yf chaunce myght take ennemies auantage fabius euer ledde hoste high place countreis styll kepynge ennemies syghte wolde farre theym yet intended giue battayle men went neuer theyr campe hylles straytes specially aboue way roman kept begynnyng nyght secretely caused men remoue campe driuing ox lytel standerdes whan came fote hyll narowe way commanded fagotes beastes horne set fyre whiche done feare flamyng fyre aboute theyr heades heate commyng quicke lower parte horne beastes caused runne though bene mad whyche sodeyne running yong roddes toke burnyng euen though woddes hylles ben fire mouing heades causing flame sprede abrode shewed like ben men runing abrode fyre whan set entryng passage sawe fyre hygh hylles aboue supposyng ben betrayde lefte place assigned theym kepe fiedde theyr succour sekyng theyr best way toppe hylles whiche great flame blase dyd shyne chaunced vpon certayne ox strayed theyr flocke whan fyrst sawe liuing thinges breathynge fyre flame stode seinge theyr enemy rather dye fielde flee incontinent slewe coulde make flee toke ouercome sparkeled abrode toke suche horse coulde get beganne flee c lentulus tribune leadyng empty horse hande fled lyfte vp kepe leste thou make battayle dolefull sorowfull throughe deathe consull without whyche veryly cause weping mournyng inough whervnto consull answered c cornelius thou increased vertue beware horseman whyche company slayne one consulles foure score senatours borne great offyce cytie whyche voluntaryly gaue theym selues battaile furthermore xxi borne office tribune besydes batayle taken iii thousande footemen iii hundred horseman roman escaped fleinge vii thousande came smaller campe x fledde greater campe whan bataile fynyshed romaynes retourned greatter campe sente whyche lesse campe partes p soone marcellus sawe hys ennemies approched walles ordered hooste wysely within walles sodeynly issued batayle makyng great noyse fyrste encountrynge dryuen backe slayne whan army ioyned marcellus greatly praysynge theyr good wylles courage commaunded stande aray redy theyr succour conuey wounded battayle shoulde wyse fyghte vntylle commaunded theym battayle stronge sowldiours fought theyr myghtes lykewyse capytaynes prouoked theym marcellus badde boldely withstande ouercomme thre dayes longe agone fledde cuma vacabundes yere dryuen nola beynge capytayne comforte theym sayde theyr enemyes battayle rouynge fieldes fought battayle wethered pleasure capua wyne hauntynge harlottes strengthes courage myghte theyr bodyes harte whyche passed greatte mountaynes called alpes hylles pyrene cleane goone sayde alsoo leauynges foresayde sowldyoures scarse able beare susteyne theyr owne membres harneys shewynge capua hurtfull displeasaunt vnto anniball menne canna romaones sayde haue lefte theyr strongthe vertue good feates warre yea haue lefte onely theyr glorye fame tyme past also hoope victorye tyme come p exhortation anniball sowldiours batayle betweene hym marcellus victory scipions spayne capitulo xxxii whan marcellus suche wordes ennemies reproche incouraged sowldiours anniball lykewyse lesse rebuke blame romanes called men sayinge knewe theym haue armour standerdes whyche hadde trebia trasymenus canna meaneth nowe saythe ye scarsely able withstande one legate romayne battayle one legyon wynge two consulles hoostes neuer able withstande shall marcellus newe vntaught souldyours succour nola yet agayne prouoke v reuenged vpon souldyours drewe flamminius horse strake heade slewe lucius paulus canna swerdes blunte youre ryghte handes astonyed wearye monstrouse thynge whyche wonte whanne ye verye fewe noumbre shorte space ouercome great meyny nowe beinge many suffer fewe stycke handes bosted bolde men tongue wold wynne rome yf man wold bryng thyther behold nowe busines moch lesse wolde ye wolde proue strength hardynesse wynnyng nola citie countrey set playne fieldes beinge compassed nother fludde sea shall leade folowe beyng laden ryche pray place euer wyll p notwithstandyng neyther reproches entisynges coulde preuayle strength theyr harte beaten backe sydes harte romanes dyd encrease onely theyr capytaynes exhortinges also nolanes steryng kyndlyng theyr courage batayle length carthaginenses fledde dryuen backe tentes marcellus brought souldiours nola great ioye thankes people whose harte inclined carthaginenses slayne day aboue theyr ennemies one thousande vi c taken standerdes baners xx iiii elephantes slayne battayle romanes slayne nexte daye truce taken whyche spente buryinge deade bodyes marcellus made oblation vulcan spoyle ennemies within thre dayes eyther displeasure hope wage ii c lxxii numidian horsmen spanyardes fledde anniball marcellus whose faithfull stronge helpe aide romanes vsed bataile often tymes anniball sent hanno agayne brusians hoste brought hym then went hym selfe wynter apulia lay arpos p soone quintus fabius harde anniball gone apulia brought corne moche thought necessary serue winter nola naples campe suessula leauyng sufficiente garry son moued campe nygh vnto capua burnyng spoylyng theyr fieldes capua constrayned trustyng lyttel theyr owne strength come citie encampe selues walles fortifyeng munimentes without gate vi souldiours armed coulde better skylle horsebacke foote wherfore horseman euer prouoked theyr enemy skyrmyshyng soone quintus fabius consull remoued tentes backe campanes myght tyll sowe theyr grounde nother dyd come thyther agayne distroye fieldes campanes new corne come vp good height able fother theyr cattall came thyther agayne caused gathered broughte claudius tentes aboue sucssula prouided wynter comaundynge marcus claudius leauynge necessary garrison nola defence therof shuld send residue sowldyours rome leste shuld bothe charge theyr frendes coste common wealthe p ende sommer whan thinges done came letter scipions great prosperous actes done spayne theyr money grayne clothynge theyr souldiours sea men spente whiche beinge pondered senate thynges necessarye ordeyned sente whan stipendes necessary come spayn towne illiturgus besieged hasdruball mago amilcar sonne bomilcar angre changed harte yelded roman neuerthelesse thorough thre hostes scipions valiantly entred towne theyr frendes without greate fyght slaughter bryngynge theym grayne good plentye wherof great nede exhorting citezens valiantly kepe defende theyr towne perceiued romaynes fyght sone issued assayle great campe wherof hasdruball capitayn thyther came succour two capitaynes carthaginenses theyr two hoostes knewe well shulde greattest battaile busynes sodeynly runnyng theyr tentes mette togyther fought carthaginenses battayle lx romaynes aboute xvi neuerthelesse battayle soo prosperous romanes page missing new man hath gotten good experience yere past newe muste put roume thinges prospere thus gouerned nowe bycause haue sufficiently spoken maner men ye ought chuse co sulles wyll speake lyttell whome fauour election hath inclyned p marcus aemilius one sacred priestes sende sacrifice shall want seruice due accustomed goddis octacilius haue maryed systers doughter haue chyldren neuerthelesse merytes desertes towardes frendes suche haue respecte common welthe priuate busynes euery maryner caulme wether rule shyppe whan sharpe stormes aryse sea beyng troubled shyppe tossed wynde nede man gouernour sayle quietly troublous stormes almost drowned therfore must prouyde great diligence shal gouerne sterne helme yea must therof take hede haue proued thy diligence octacilius lesser busynes wherin truely thou dyddest deserue shulde committe greatter charge thre cause sent furthe nauy laste yere thou gouernour fyrst border affrica shuld haue bene wasted distroyed seconde hauens strondes italy shulde haue ben kepte safe v thynges succour stypende necessary beinge sent carthage anniball shulde haue free passage content ye make octacilius consull yf proue dyd performe common welth thynges hym comytted yf thou capytayn nauy sent carthage anniball free passage though sea bene open border italy yere indaungered border affrica canst thou alledge thy selfe thou shuldest chosen chiefe capytayne agaynst anniball appertayneth man octacilius take heede suche burthen layde thy necke weyght wherof wyll peise downe admonyshe perswade chosynge consul tyme ye vse circumspection ye wolde vse yf ye dryuen chose twayne gouerne bataile wente newe election quintus fabius hym selfe created fourth tyme consul marcus marcellus thyrd time created without variance nother man suspect quintus fabius couetousnes rule gouernace rather praised noblenes courage hart whan sawe common welthe dyd want good capytayne knewe hym selfe withoute doubte one estemed enuy shulde haue yf shulde aryse matter lesse profyt comon welth p whan thynges hym made greater spede come thyther roman whan hadde bene season lefte certayne numidian spanyardes defende citie wente hym selfe lake auernus vnder colour make sacrifyce withstandyng pretence set puteolus left garryson p whan fabius maximus hearde anniball gone arpos tourned agayne campania without restyng nyght day went hest caused gracchus remoue frome luceria beneuentum made quintus fabius sonne abyde place luceria hym selfe came cassilinum intendyng besiege carthaginenses therein tyme thynge appoynted hanno came brusianes great host horsmen fotemen beneuentu chanced titus gracchus came luceria thyther somwhat hym entred towne whan hearde hanno pitched tentes iii mile towne water called calor wasted countrey went hym selfe towne pytched tentes myle ennemy assemble souldiours wherof moste part bondemen bene warre yere bondemen thought theyr desertes made free wold desyre openly withstandyng perceyued murmure ofthem complaynyng sayinge shall neuer free battaile like free souldiours citezens wherof wrote letter senate well desyre deseruyng sayinge euer vnto day theyr good faithful strong helpe wanted nothing belonged good iust souldiours sauing liberty co cerning matter permitted vnto whiche shuld thinke mete profite comon welth whervpon wold battaile aduersarye shewed men tyme come whiche might opteyne theyr libertie longe desyred hoped nexte day shuld fyght fayre playne fielde battayle shulde done without feare disceyte cleane strengthe hardynes wold shewe head one ennemies stryken battaile shuld streight way made free fledde shuld punished vile seruitude euer wherfore nowe sayde euery man fortune lyeth owne handes confirmation whiche wordes said alone auctour theyr lybertie marcus marcellus consull father conscripte agreable thereof sente hym theyr letter whiche shewed red vnto wordes arose great noyse amonge desyryng battaylle incontynent yf myghte soo please hym gracchus lette conuocation passe appoynted battayle agaynste nexte daye souldyours verye gladde especiall whyche supposed theyr wage one day perpetuall libertie p battayle betwene hanno gracchus rewarde also punyshement awarded gracchus certayne bondemen hoost capi xxxiiii nexte daye whan trumpettes blewe battayle came togyther good araye anone vppon sonne rysynge gracchus broughte sowldyours battayle theyr ennemyes made taryeng theyr part xvii thousande footemen one ii hundred horseman battayle sharpe lasted iiii howres knowynge whiche shulde haue victorye nothynge troubled romanes heades theyr ennemyes whyche gracchus appoynted pryce theyr libertie wherfore euer stryken downe theyr ennemies wolde strike heade beare theyr handes stede weapon whyche thynge gracchus apperceyuynge commaunded euery man shulde leaue head hand take weapon fyghte naturall site therof beyng halfe compassed sea beatyng great hygh rockes halfe hauing great dyches hyghe walles towarde towne lothe spende tyme assaultyng therof leaue great thynges folowed castynge romaynes wolde aduenture make excursion labourer lette worke purpose intended yf fiersely wold dispose men pryuily imbushmentes slaughter shulde made shoulde able hurte towne euen thoughte soo camme passe soone worke begunne anone gate castell sette open romaynes came workemen carthaginenses suche violence anone gaue backe sommewhat purposely enhaunce theyr harte courage allure theym frome theyr holde anone certayne token gyuen imbusshemente brake suche force inuaded romaynes fledde backe moche speede towarde castelle strete soo narowe whyche muste passe soo troubled baggage labourer laye waye many slayne fleinge fyghtynge thus power castell lefte small afterwarde theyr workes neuer lette depe dyche walle made suche wyse neded leaue garryson towne neuer lesse theyr sauegarde lefte certayn souldiours reste army remoued fyue myles thense ryuer galesus pitched tentes soone retourned viewe strength castell thought myght wonne saute whervppon caused maner engyns made sette vp agaynste walles greatte feare theym castell sodeynly nyghte came certayne shyppes menne warre frome metapontus whyche holden roman entred hauen whose healpe castell threwe downe burned ingynes munymentes carthaginenses wherby anniball loste hope wynnynge castelle assaulte ymagyned contynuall siege famysshe theym whyche purpose also serued hym nothynge castelle hadde sea free oone syde receyued vytayles theyr plesure romaynes beynge maysters hauen kepte prouysyon frome cytie wonte comme water soo moche lyke endure famyne thanne castelle whome besieged wherfore anniball mystrusting strength place called ruler tarent hym sayde p beholde nature site strengthe castell see assault preuayle long ennemies lordes sea haue liberty may said haue shippes may restrain vitailes brought either wil depart then yeld vnto v tarentines agreed well said must helpe nauy carthage sicilia might caused comme thither kepe said port sayde anniball haue shyppes owne yes truely sayde lye littell creke longe ennemies haue dominion mouthe hauen howe euer escape brode sea yes said anniball feare many thinges naturally letted witte policy may brought passe citie situate playne euen grounde stretes way brode passe partes shippes wyll conuey high way leadeth middell citie vpon waines wheles vnto hauen smalle charge sea shall nowe enemy lordes sea lande wyll compasse shortely shall dryuen forsake castell el shall take bothe also p wyse diuise made men haue wonder admiration hym also hoope good successe purpose furth withal wayne carte gathered tyed togither engins made raise drawe vp shippes way made hard euen leuell myght easily drawen thus strength beastes men shyppes broughte hauen fewe day garnished men thinges necessary brought rounde castell castyng ankers mouthe hauen p fuluius flaccus romane consull wynneth campe hanno sleeth taketh great number men ryche pray mago sleeth titus gracchus many romaynes treason flauius lucan capitu xxxvi vvhyles anniball thus occupied aboute busynesse tarent quintus fuluius flaccus appius claudius chosen consul yere com bothe armyes party samnite ruler capua feared greatly lest dyd intende shortly besiege citie also plentye corne beganne faile legion roman hadde inuaded countrey campanes durst neither tyll sow groundes wherfore sent legate vnto annibal desiring hym cause plenty wheate brought capua countrey adioynyng consul dydde enter countrey theyr army whervpon anniball sent messangers hanno shuld come brusians army capania make prouision campanes might haue good plenty corne sent p hanno commaunded leauynge samnite consul passed tyll came within iii myles beneuentum mountayne pitched campe townes frendes adioyning great plentie wheate sommer bene caryed made goodly prouision campanes sent worde secretely capua day shuld wayne carte coulde assemble countrey resorte sayd place fette away said wheate campanes lyghtly sklenderly foreseing busines welth day assigned came thither bringyng iiii hundred carte theyr slouth hanno greatly rebuked maruaylyng wolde hedily auoyde hunger whiche brute beastes labour eschue wherfore sente home laden appoynted nother day retourne againe moche greatter quantitie p appoyntment came eares beneuentanes whervpon incontynent sente tenne messangers consulles certifyenge theym campanes purpose furthwith agreed fuluius armye shoulde goo beneuentum enter towne nyghte kepynge close therin tyll sawe tyme apte purpose soone fuluius entred beneuentum shewed hym hanno parte army gone furth wheate ii wayns come campe great rude sort people vnarmed lay myngled amonge souldiours kepyng order vse men warre knowen consul comanded men redy theyr baners armure next night wold assayle campanes tentes carthaginenses executyng commandement made redy iiii clocke set furthe towne came hannos campe lyttell dawnyng day theyr fyrst commynge sodain noise carthaginenses becam feareful campe pitched plain ground wonne small resistence height hyll defeses made therabout could way get vp vnto great steppe climming daunyng day bataile began waxe stronge carthaginenses onely defended campe also kept hyll without euer throwing doune roma stroue wondersly clymme place neuerthelesse length great pein trauaile also great losse hurt men gat diches campe consull aduisyng well mischief shulde fall company winning place callid tribune vnto saying wold time pursue folishe enterprise wold returne day beneuentu morow wold ioyne campe campe enmies campanes shuld issue hanno haue recours whan returned bring better surely passe wolde sende felowe claudius consull army assist therin whan tribune caused retreate sowned souldiours earnestly busy aboute enterprise wolde gyue none care therto among one vibius capitain copany pelignes streight toke baner hande force threwe ouer diche campe carthaginenses sayd euyl might fare company myn enemy shall enioy baner great force lightly went ouer diche clame vp entred campe enemy company boldly folowed thus fought within cape carthaginenses part cried valerius flaccus sluggishe cowardes nowe waxen shall pelignes wynne honour taking campe ennemies v roman whervpon titus pedanius capitayn hudred men toke standerd hande standerde bearer saying standerde wyll beare fielde myne enemy folowe syrs many wolde lothe losse therof anone companye goten part cape consul perceyuing hardynes changed mynd calling away began comfort exhorting rest helpe felowes valiantly fought campe theyr enmies whose harty wordis euery man inforced selfe enter regarding dartes weapon enemy people fearyng peryll people cared deth might dye campe enemy thus within short space strong place wone aboue vi slayn vii taken men campania came corne al carte riche pray ha gotten fieldes frendes roman whiche pray consul solde tyme claudius also come thither therwith rewarded men specially vibius pedanius whan hanno hearde losse people fledde backe againe brutianes fewe men whiche taken hym get wheate campanes p capanes heryng losse men frendes sent annibal shewing cosuls beneuentu within day iorney capua intending lay siege city feared lest shortly succour roman wold wynne distroy citie said nother castell tarent town also ought moch estemed capua noblenes wherof knew well selfe moch wont compare vnto carthage wherfore trusted wold leaue vndefended haue spoiled distroyed romayns p annibal hering message shewed ambassadours loue bare vnto citie promising euer defender therof gentyll wordes sent home sent also ii horsmen whose helpe might defend fieldes robbing wastyng p meane whyle p cornelius pretor certain shippes laden wheate came hauen tarent hole power carthaginenses caused also suche souldiours metapontus garrison come castell tarent remaine defence therof whose cominge castell sure hurt ennemies soone inhabitantes metapontus deliuered romayne garrison incontinent fell leage amitie anniball whervpon thurines also hauynge grudge roman sleing diuers frendes aforsaid deuysed meane bringe citie amitie anniball kynsmen slayne sente messangers hanno mago among brusians willing come army lay siege towne doubtyng one marcus attinius ruler smalle company romaynes left defence towne wolde anon brought issue gyue battaylle vppon trust yong men armes towne armed instructed feates warre roman facion douted sort wold doo hym small pleasure whan shuld haue nede theym two capitains hearing glad tidinges spede entred fieldes thurines diuydyng company betwene theym hanno footemen baners displayed good aray went towarde towne mago horsmen abode valey vnder certayn hylles nigh towne attinius knowing company foteme put men good aray great courage issued towne nothing mystrustyng myschiefe wrought agaynst hym within towne battaile quicke part roman thurines stode men gaue lokynge enemy hanno men pourpose gaue backe drawe romanes daunger horsmen whan came nere hilles fiersly assayled romayns syde mago horseman came sodainly egrely vpon fyrst encountring thurines fledde towne fast coulde roman season mainteyned battaile last constrained thereto also fledde towarde towne traytours causers al mischief gotten gate power commyng backe thurines fledde kept open gate receyued towne whan romanes came fleyng also thinkyng haue entred cried tyme nowe shutte gate el shall lette carthaginenses towne among owne men lose whervpon shut theyr gate suffred roman slayne ennemies without succour attinius capitayn gentilly dered ruler suffered enter fewe incontinent gaue shippe hauen badde hym saue selfe sea whose departynge opened gate receyued carthaginenses p nowe consul departed beneuentu assaute capua thinkyng shuld make yere happy honourable yf might wynne capua noble riche reuenge iniuries done neuerthelesse intent beneuentanes shulde lefte withoute succour theyr absence sent titus gracchus cuntrey lucans commandyng hym horseman lyght footemen come beneuentum leauynge lucanes reste men vnder capitayn myght truste p lucans diuided diuers townes rendred vp anniball certaine abode vnder romaynes iurisdiction sort chiefe rular yere one flauius lucan flauius sodeynly tourned mynde anniball obteyne fauour sente mago among brutians come speke hym whan mette composition made betwene coulde delyuer gracchus capitayn romain army lucanes shulde frendly receiued amitie carthagineses lyue lawes tha brought mago great couert willed great numbre men armes hyde hym appoyntyng hym tyme whiche wolde bring thither romaine capitayne appoyntment departed went gracchus shewed begunne secretely great enterpryse whyche brynge effecte muste haue healpe assystence haue sayde moued perswaded pryncis lucans gone amitie anniball nowe retourne agayne obedience rome haue declared vnto increase romanes power whiche dayly may perceiue decrease strength carthaginenses bad mystrust gentylnes romains whose nature haue euer tryed meke gentyll suche haue rebelled agaynst vpon hu ble submissio made persuasion contented reconciled may speake laying right hand pledge faithe whervnto may trust haue sayde vndertaken shall doo haue appoynted composition secrete place wel way company feare espies yet far campe fewe wordes may go matter meane bryng lucanes wholly vnder iurisdiction p gracchus nothyng strustynge disceite treason wordes toke officer horseman al vnarmed rode place appointed hauynge flauius hym guyde soone come thyther mago army inuaded theym sodaynly make treason euident flauius incontinent ioyned carthaginenses plenty dartes caste gracchus horseman whan sawe noo remedy alyght horse bad company doo exhortynge syns fewe number vnarmed suche place coulde noo waye escape wolde dye lyke beastes vnreuenged noble harte shoulde assaile theyr ennemyes dye bathed besprynkled bloudde theyr ennemies whereby shulde ende moste honour specially aboue thyng sayde lette euery v seeke slea lucane traytour flauius doubtynge euer shall sende traytours soule helle dye hym selfe shall fynd oblation therof todoo hym moche comforte solace soone hadde thus spoken threwe clooke aboute lefte arme stede shielde ranne vppon ennemies dartes weapon slewe part romaine whan sawe gracchus without helpe intended take hym lyue soone perceiued flauius amonge ennemies ranne thickest suche force haue slayne constrained slea hym elles done greate hurte whose body mago caused brought anniball caused buried moche honour p centenius penula cneius fuluius theyr two army discomfyted horseman healpe townes men issued oute sodaynely theym euer coulde gather togyther order battaile slewe one thousand fyue hundred losse caused consul circumspectly worke theyr procedynges afterwarde p harte began fayle whervpon lesius yererular citie called generall counsayle whyche many senatours moued ambassadours shulde sent romayn consul vibius virius chiefe causer yeldyng capua anniball beynge demaunded opinyon therin aunswered spake peace takyng yeldyng capua ought remembre bothe wolde haue done yf romayns theyr power lyke case also campanes lyke suffer whan submitted wholly theyr pleasure p lette v sayde remembre howe leauing theyr frendshyp submytted v anniball contented therwith slewe romaynes lefte garrison v haue certayne knowlege theyr harte enuy towarde v lette v call v theyr actes done late agaynst v therby ye shall perceyue kyndnes lyke haue theyr handes anniball straunger theyr vtter enemy italy cuntrey partes fulfylled warre yet leauyng anniball theyr busynesse sente bothe consulles theyr whole armyes besiege capua longe contynuall kepyng siege almost famished hunger profe theyr yee towarde v let v consyder although anniball commyng succour almoste wonne theyr campes sayne many theyr men put great ieopardy losing yet ieoperdous peryll losse neuer coulde moue theym remoue theyr siege afterward whan passed riuer vulturnus bournynge fieldes calenus theyr fath full frendes yet coulde hurtes call capitaynes myserable siege ye caused baners displayd walles citie rome saying onles wold leaue capua wold take high citie rome yet wolde leaue siege capua beares wulues wyld beastes neuer great rage fury man goo caues theyr yong whelpes lye anone wyll leaue al aboute runne streighte defence theyr yonge furyous romaynes whan rome compassed theyr enemy nother theyr wyues chyldren whose lamentable wepinges myght heard almoste hither nother house temple goddis feare violating sepulture theyr auncetours coulde withdrawen siege capua desyrous execute v greuous punyshement sore thyrst drynke bludde reason happily shulde haue done lykewyse yf fortune deserued v wherfore sen pleasure goddis nedes muste dye yet wylle chuse deathe bothe honest gentyll wherby wyll escape tormentes dispites myne ennemies truste put vnto whan fuluius claudius shall solempnely triumph enter rome wyl bounden drawen spectacle wondryng stocke put pryson tyed poste suffer body scourged last haue head stryken body axe rome nother lyue se cuntrey distroied bourned see noble matron maiden capua rauished defouled beginnyng flourishynge citie rome romains distroyed citie alba threwe downe grounde yet theyr originall citie trowe ye wyl capua whiche hate doo carthage therfore frendes many desyrous dye ye se many spiteful misery come day dyner meate alredy dressed wha well filled wyne good meates cup drynke wyll fyrst drinke selfe shall borne euery one drynke shall delyuer body tormentes mynde rebuke eies eares fro syght hearyng cruell dispites prepared people ouercome whan shall deade seruauntes shall redy throwe body great fyres made purpose bourned shall neuer come handes enemy onely honest free way dye wherby ennemies shall meruaile wonder noble courage annibal shal therby well perceyue hath forsaken betrayde valyant faithfull felowes p oration vibius heard wel alowed many mo harte folowe put execution part senatours said oft tymes warres experience pitie gentylnesse romaine shewed ennemies suche extremitie mystrustyng shulde fynde mercyfull nowe vpon humble request made thervpon determined send legatis cosul yeld vp capua p vibius virius went home enbrasyng one lamented owne deathes distruction cuntrey remained died bourned fyres made intent went home house made ende towne deliuered romaine none left lyue p next day gate opened romaine suffered enter gate kepte romains man shuld go furth first armour wepons brought romain capitain carthaginenses garrison taken put prison senatours comanded go consul tentes whens consenting receiuig annibal sent sudry prison xxv cales xxviii theanus vntil agreed punishment shuld haue golde syluer brought deliuered officer called questores claudius co sull moch inclined take senator mercy fuluius side wold haue suffer example rebelles traytours wherefore claudius remitted thing iugement senate rome sent thither knowe pleasure therin whervpon fuluius fearing lest shuld stayed purpose comanded tribune ii horseman redy ride third blast trumpet copany horsmen night departed army day light came theanus causyng senatours capua prisoner brought incontinent caused violently scourged roddes haue heades striken then fast might hied cales likewise sat vpon iugement senatours capua while going execution one came senate rome riding great hast letter willing stay iudgement execution punishment capane senator fuluius iudging letter writen intent neuer disclosed put bosom saying officer shuld procede quickly execution accordinge lawe also whipped heades stryken consull drewe furth letter redde saying came late let thynge alredy done cales returned capua put diuers prison beside many citie sold tha great debate senate rome whether citie capua shuld burned vtterly dystroyed exaumple rebelles moch moued theym soo doo greate stronge citie nere neyghbour vnto whych shuld ennemy agayne rome late greatlye dysquiete romaynes neuerthelesse conclusyon considering fertilitie grounde marcus marcellus wel proued experience chosen consull appointed match anniball concerning warres italy marcus valerius leuinus elect consull thende warres sicilia wholly comitted industry treason diuided iii army gouerned thre capitaines asdruball sonne gysgon mago two capitaines lay v dayes iourney romaine legion thyrd whiche asdruball sonne amilcar auncient capitayne carthaginenses countreye laye anniturgium neerevnto romaine hadde pourpose sommer folowynge passe mountaynes conueye armye anniball pourpose lette two scipio thought fyrste assayle hym aloone company doubtyng stronge inough doo greattest feare lest whan ouercome hasdruball mago hearyng therof wolde flee mountaynes straytes power prolonge warres spayn wherfore make ende theyr trouble one concluded part army twayne p cornelius two partes shulde goo agaynst two capitaines lay togither cn scipio thyrde part theyr olde army celtiberians shulde assaile asdruball sonne amilcar mindes set furth togither toward ennemies cn scipio whan came aniturgium rested company syght enemy hauyng riuer betwene hym brother went furthe agreed betwene asdruball perceiuing numbre romayns small strengthe stranger late hyred knowing faccion people vntrue vnstable meane spaniardes coulde speake language great summes money corrupted princis rulars agreed departe home theyr hole power desyred hyred vndertake warres asdrubal romaine onely depart without fighting whervnto sone intreated partly large wage though shuld haue foughten agayne gladde retourne home theyr cuntreys frendes auoyding danger warre therfore sodaynely baners caryage departed romaine meruayling sodaine chaunge ment enquired cause departure answered sent home defende theyr owne cuntrey whiche oppressed also warre answere could none gette nother romaynes able kepe force scipio knowyng without theym nothynge able encounter asdruball also seynge waye howe myghte recouer companye brother ennemies beinge soo nere commynge hym meruaylously astonied yet thought beste wyse meete hym euen grounde soo farre ouermatched wherfore lyttell lyttell drewe backe sekyng place strength myghte succour hym selfe small company perceiuing hasdruball passed ryuer hooste folowed moche speede could p nowe p scipio brother moche troubled parte reason massanissa yong lusty prince numidia beinge frende carthaginenses comme good power numidian succour mago hasdruball sonne gysgon fiers greatte courage romaynes coulde nother goo abrode vitayles woode suche necessary numidian euer redy oppresse dyuers tymes nyght wolde assayle theym theyr campe people besieged also tydinges brought scipio one indibilis seuen thousande fyue hundred suessanes hande commynge healpe carthaginenses whose army beinge ioyned knewe shulde straightly enclosed wherfore compelled necessitie serche compasse wytte determyned secretely take greatter part armye meete indibilis nyghte intendynge soo euer mette hym gyue hym battaylle lefte titus fonteius certayne hym keepe campe goynge waye aboute mydnyght met indibilis sodaynly assayled hym fyerse conflycte season sodayne settynge theym romaynes hadde putte theym flyghte greatte slaughter hadde numidian horsemenne alwayes awayted romaynes soo euer wente bothe partes sodeynly assayled theym yet scipio soo pryuily nyght departed hadde thought therby haue begiled numidian watchemen battail renued agayn mago asdruball hostes folowing theyr backes romaynes knew whiche best tourne scipio stille comforted exhorted men euer battaile moste stronge thyther went lyke noble valiant gouernour tyll last hym selfe thyrst ryght syde speare fell dead hors whan carthaginenses sawe romayne capitayne falle incontinent ranne abrode partes fielde ioyfully cryinge scipio capitayne romaine slayne fame wherof gaue hart carthaginenses caused romaynes flee flyght mo slayne batail numidian horsmen fierse chase footemen hauyng lyght harneis almost swyft horse yf nyght come theym fewe none escaped carthaginenses victory slept stayde folowe theyr good occasyon offered incontinent toke theyr horse went hasdruball sonne amilcar doutyng good spede also theyr power mette togyther great ioye made betweene capiteynes bothe theyr metynge also newes theyr late victory p syde romayns stryken feareful pensifenes knowlege losse company spede made theyrennemies worde thereof coulde soone broughte feare inwarde secrete iudgement theyr harte somme euyll chaunce happed vnto theym agayne cn scipio seing hoste ennemyes encreased commynge mago asdruball meruailed howe shulde conuey theyr armye thyther soone without battayle onlesse brother slayne meruayled alsoo brother nother dydde lette commynge thyther nother yet dydde appere folowynge theym knewe yf lyne wolde make haste come ioyne army vnto great trouble mynde thoughte withdrawe hym moche myght wherefore nyght gone good space grounde dawnyng daye numidian ware departing folowed horse long nyght ouertoke theym assayling one side somtyme behynde euer scipio caused theym keepe good aray go euer forewarde fightynge daunger footemen enemy folowed horseman vexed partes could go farre wherfore scipio gathered small company vp lytell hyll best coulde espy aduatage toke order theyr stuffe cariage brought myddell host horseman sette without foote men saued inuasion numidian horseman tyl rest carthaginenses come scipio seing hym selfe vnable resist iii capitaynes great hostes began diuise howe might meanes cast trenche campe make hedge defende inuasions theyr enemy tha hyll bare grounde stony bush thornes coulde gathered turues dygged trenche made hyll selfe flatte coulde maner way let commyng vp enemy scipio make shewe defence aboute campe deuised lay packes grosse cariage co passe campe one vpon thervppon caused packsaddels fardel tyed wherby raysed walles campe good height p whan hostes carthaginenses come ascended small hyll lyttel peyne seing straunge kynde fortifieng campe neuer sene amased stayde season capitaynes perceiuyng theyr sodayne stoppe wondryng cried al partes saying great shame longe coulde plucke downe deface suche fond deuise mockery wherwith child woman wold long haue ben stayed go therfore courage sayd ennemies lye lurkyng behynde packes rebuke capitaines assayed enter partes though greate whyle lette troubled therabout last diuers partis entred numbre could longer endure many campe wonne many slain wherof cn scipio noble capitayne one good number sledde woodes next vnto escaped came tentes publius scipio whyche kept fonteius thus bothe bretherne capytaynes romaynes spayne slayne within space xxx dayes whose death greatly lamented rome also spain thought death hole army romaine spayn vtterly brought confusyon countrey thereby brought romaynes handes p l martius chosen capitaine romaine army maketh oration souldiours one nyghte day vanquisheth ii hostes carthaginenses winneth campes greate praye capit xlii peryll ieoperdous estate one man founde army whose witte courage fortune honour welthe romaynes saued restored lucius martius sonne septinius freshe yonge man actiue martius hadde longe ben warres vnder c scipio hym learned moche experience policy gouernance army nowe seing thinges almoste desperate gathered togither souldiours fleing escaped last bataile also assembled good numbre men warre dyuers townes fortress whiche vnder obedience rome came tentes fonteius ioynyng romaine power togither short space name honour exalted whole consent souldyours army chosen capitayne guyde whervpon incontinent applied himselfe busyly make sure theyr campe also make good prouisyon vitayles sortes whose pleasure commaundement men hoste gladly obeyed neuerthelesse whan hearde hasdruball sonne gysgon hande army myndynge dystroye vtterly romaynes lefte also whan sawe theyr newe capitayne makynge redy people auauncyng standerdes remembryng theyr olde noble capytaines great power wherwith wont go batayles coulde forbeare wepe lament theyr myshappe suche wyse nother theyr pety capitaynes yet martius hym selfe myght appease yet dyd sometime rebuke theyr feminine vnprofitable wepinges sometyme styrre defende selues countrey also reuenge deathe theyr olde noble capitaynes late slayne whyle thus spendyng tyme vnprofytably theyr ennemies hande redye assaile enter campes romaine tournyng teares furious rage haste toke armure weapon defended entry campe also issued fiersely ranne ennemies whiche kepte good aray littell mystrusted resistence sodayne issuing caused carthaginenses striken feare also meruaile howe romaine hoste shortly encreased whiche late almooste wholly slayn put vtterance mused also sodayne courage hardynesse newe capytaine myght haue truste two scipio beinge slaine feare dout beganne somwhat giue backe romaine folowed vppon soo constrayned flee flyght many hadde bene slayne elles folowers hadde bene putte greatte hurte dyspleasure theyr faste pursuite hadde martius hym selfe sounde retreate halfe agaynste theyr wylles stayed theym frome chase broughte theym backe theyr tentes beynge styll hotte fyerse desyrous slaughter reuenge theym enenmies carthaginenses fledde faste season laste seynge noo manne folowe thought feare durste noo longer pursue theym wherefore made noo suche haste wente softely theyr campe whanne come thither also regarded greatly good watche kepynge therof lefte thinges negligently vnsurely nothynge mystrusting ennemies hande demed remenaunt leauynges two hostes lately beaten nowe beynge gathered togyther neglygence carthaginenses knowen martius espies wherefore fyrste apparance semed rather rasshely boldly enterpryse night folowinge inuade theym theyr tentes fielde thinking easye wynne campe hasdruball alone beinge sodainly taken vnprouided shoulde able defende owne campe fielde taried tyll iii capitaines carthaginenses theyr arinies ioyned togither agayne neuerthelesse wold sodainly night time enterprise high feate thought fyrst make companye priuie therof also make vnto oration whiche began wise p greatte loue haue euer borne vnto oure good capytaynes louynge souldiours welle whan onlyue also nowe deade presente fortune tyme sufficient perswade man greatte authoritie rule goodnes ye haue gyuen weighty full care trouble although mynde sore troubled disquieted almoste tyme fynde comfort consolation onely whan feare dryueth away sorowes thereof yet dolour onely constrayned comforte relieue sorowes neyther whan deuysynge meanes may saue preserue leauynges two romaine hostes wealthe countrey tyme quitte ridde sorowes euen thanne two scipio bothe daye nyghte doo vexe trouble sommetyme dreames appeere vnto many tymes awake slepes comanding leaue yet noble souldiours copanions comon welth vnreuenged intent folow rule discipline haue taught while lyuing man obedient commandement tha lykewyse ar departed shall always glad thyng suppose wold haue done yf werehere v lyuing wold ye shuld thynke best worthy warriours mourne weepe theym though cleane deade sen lyue perpetually noble fame honorable actes whan euer ye shall going battayle remembre wolde haue vahantly fight though ye sawe setting furthe baners displayde exhortyng wyn honour imagination caused yesterday manfully vanquysshe put flyght youre enemy wherfore moche desyrous proue whether hardy owne pleasure dare vndertake moche desyre exhortation youre capitayne yesterday whan called backe chase enmies dyd plucke downe stomakes quench noble courage deferre greatter honour also better oportunitie intente beinge prepared therfore may assayle theym vnpurueyde armed may take vnarmed slepe enemy thinke nothyng lesse beinuaded v campe whome accompt people besieged within owne campe let v nowe therfore enterpryse whiche man thinke dare enterpryse shall founde moste easy semed moste harde compassed selfe wyll guide dead night leade secretly suche silence wyll within theyr campe er shalbe ware comming ascertained kepe watche order campe shall wyn fyrst brunt let see make slaughter amonge intended yesterday haue made wha wylles called back fro pursuit wherwith ye angry enterprise know great hardy suche necessitie suche cou sels best whan occasion offred oportunitie serueth muste taken el wyll flee away without recouerie one theyr army hande two farre hense nowe yf assayle one hoste may fynde oportunitie haue equall matche ye haue alredy yesterday assayed bothe owne strength
