affyrme true nother saye false vntrewe couertly left dwell styll theyr owne opinion wherby men suche admiration hym suffred hym enioy great roume el full vnmete yong age army shuld vnder hym spayne increased tenne thousand fotemen one horseman iulius sullanus appoynted helpe hym busy affayres charge p newe army nauy xxx shyppes departed italy makyng great spede tylle arryued spayne gathered togither power remained sobrely handled self al men woordes iudged bothe royall maiestie stedfast faythfulnes praysed moch souldiours whiche founde fyrst withstanding theyr ii great loss men capitayns yet kept still cuntrey defendyng manfully frendis many city also suffred theyr ennemies enioy prosperous fortune whiche losse romayns one gyuen thyrdly driuen ennemies forsake theyr abode lide water iberus aboue lucius martius great honour veneration anon comyng bestowed newe menne warre place shuld remaine winter season hym selfe thinges ordinately disposed went tarracon p fame scipio lesse among ennemies tha among frendes also certaine feare hym coniecturyng secrete diuination likely successe thynges ensue feared hym hadde cause feared hym moche cause reason theyr feare hydde vnknowen perplexitie mynde departed army went dyuers partes wynter season hasdruball sonne gysgon went sea toward pyllars hercules mago kept myddell cuntrey hasdruball sonne amilcar lay nigh riuer iberus farre sagunt p oration scipio souldyours spayne commyng thyther cap xliiii spryng yere p scipio comanded shyppes furnished men vitailes munimentes warre mete hym mouthe ryuer iberus rest hoste cominge lande tarracon mette thinkyng necessary hym declare mynde olde souldyours lefte spayne laste great losse slaughter romaynes called togyther made oration hereafter foloweth p neuer newe capitayn cause gyue thankes vnto souldyours hadde tryed theyr hardines diligence bataile fortune hath boud vnto louinge souldiours knewe countreye sawe place campe fyrste loue obedience ye haue borne father mine vncle bothe quycke deade secundarily whan hole countrey loste reason greate distruction people yet noble vertue myghte haue obteyned possession agayne bothe romaynes also theyr deputie successour sayd father vncle sen fauour goddis intende worke may dwell spayne styll selues carthaginenses shall haue dwellyng nother onely restraine shall come syde bankes water iberus intend passe floode army gyue battayle feare lest shall thoughte counsayle hardy spoken myne age wyse consyderynge late losse haue wherby tyme shuld serue v vndertake suche great enterpryses noo manne hath cause remembre euyll fortune batayle spayne haue father myne vncle slayne within space thyrty day ye wold say make heape corp family one vpon neuerthelesse losse lacke frendes displeasant mynde men euen doth fortune noble vertuouse courage forbyd man suche case dispayre specially sen thorough fatall fortune chaunce hath heretofore bene haue bene beaten susteined great loss beginning yet last haue euer ouercome ennemies suppressed v wyll reherse olde hystories warres porsena frenchman samnite wyll onely remembre warres ennemies carthaginenses many nauies shyppes howe many capitaynes howe many army lost fyrst battayles theym tyme anniball nowe tyme trebia trasymenus canna thinges appere hole armyes theyr capitaynes romayne consul slayne furthermore howe great parte italy sardinia sicilia haue forsaken romaynes folowe amitie anniball nigh citie rome pytched campe ye hym self sene almost ride hard gate rome tyme great ruyne hard fortune hertes vertue courage romaynes remayned styl stedfast hole vnmouable wherby haue ben euer susteyned set vp agayne cruell batayle canna hasdruball great armye goynge ouer mountaynes italye helpe brother anniball ioyne theyr power together whych done accordynge intent hadde thys day ben almost memorye name romayns left ye hardy souldyours gouernaunce father withstode theim good fortune wel sped therby euel chaunces hapned v wel releued nowe goodnes goddes dayly ioyfull prosperous sicilia great city syracusa agrigentum wonne agayn hole ile brought vnto obedience romaine ennemies clene expulsed italy capua taken arpines brought vnder subiection rome anniball gret feare fleing fro rome nowe bryuen angle countrey brutians dayly prayer maketh goddes aboue al thinges may safe sound escape without daunger countrey ennemies wherfore frendes nothyng vnmete contrary reason haue al aduersitie lowe ebbe goddes selues almost annibals partie yet guyding father frendes haue susteyned borne vp estate romaynes ye nowe al thynges ar mery prosperous shoulde shrynke suffre harte fayle nowe immortall goddes gouernours romayne empyre wylled people rome one assent elect vnto gret offyce dignitie goddes sundry presage signes dreames nyght haue shewed thynges hereafter shal haue prosperous successe ye time regarde harte giueth ere long al spaine shalbe many beare name carthaginense shall gladde feare flee hen lande sea reason also gyueth whiche herte conceyued must nedes trewe dyuers theyr frendes whyche haue theym ben euil intreted haue late sent embassadours v socours agayne thre captaines whiche agree among selues whiche cause haue deuided theyr armye three partes departed farre sundre wherfore fortune skourged distroyed v doth nowe come theim felowes friendes trust gone theim euen people called celtiberi departed forsoke hadde moste nede theim also haue deuided seuered theyr hostes cause destruction bothe father myne vncle discorde wyll suffer theim ioyne gether againe ye sure one armie theim selfe able withstande wherfore moste hertely pray good souldiours loue fauour nowe name scipions whiche sonne olde capitaine scipio impe growen ye woulde saye stocke cut downe grounde ye olde knightes worke ye may brynge yonge capitaine newe armie ouer iberus countrey ye haue passed many great actes prowes shewed doubte shortly bringe passe ye nowe knowe similitude resemblaunce father vncle face countenaunce feature body euen shall ye see also exaumple theyr witte faith vertue suche wyse euery one shall saye scipio olde capitaine alyue agayne p citie newe carthage hispayne romaynes great praye golde siluer necessary warre pledge noble menne city spayne capi xlv vvhen exhortation kendeled hertes men lefte behinde hym kepe countreye sillanus three thousande fotemen thre hundred horseman rest armye xxv thousande fotemen ii thousande v c horseman passed ryuer iberus passed ouer many counsailed hym seinge army carthaginenses deuydedinto thre partes shulde assaile host theim next vnto hym sayenge peryll ioyned together lest shulde able resyste theim imagined mynde woulde fyrste assaulte carthago noua whiche onely ryche rychesse inhabitantes also riche meanes carthaginenses leyde theyr treasure armour moche apparayll warre remayned also citie pledge noble men citees spayne besyde citie situate vpon sea whense easy passe ouer affrica hauen also therof able receyue easely greatest nauye prynce p purpose man priuye onely lelius gouernour shyppes armye sea whome commaunded soo tempre course shyppes armye lande sea myghte bothe sodaynely appeere carthage one tyme whyche charge dewely putte execution seuenthe daye theyr departynge frome iberus mette newe carthage incontynente campe made tentes pytched northe syde citie p nowe syte sytuation carthage manier myddell spayne greatte bosome goulfe whyche sea hath full course within lande lengthe fyue hundred pass breadthe sea place muche quantitie inner parte furthest ende goulfe hylle whyche citie buylded two partes saye easte syde southe syde enclosed sea whyche frome sayde goulfe bosome rounneth lande one syde citie vppon weaste syde defended greatte brode poole rounneth vp also good part northe syde towne deepenesse poole noo certayntie sea dothe aryse heyghte ebbe lowe soo water thereof deepe shalowe p thus cytie partes enuyronned water ylande oneles part northsyde mayne lande passeth ii hundred fyfty pace bredth wherfore sen grounde broder scipio intended make trench part thought hym selfe stronge ynough keepe lyttell peece grounde ennemies also thintent myght tymes haue recourse view walles strength towne p whan scipio ordered thinges ordinately vpon lande assaulte went hauen lyke maner ordered shippes men might appere citizen shoulde assaulted well water lande also commaunded watche kepte vpon water night season euery shyppe thynges prudently appoynted retourned campe wyllyng dyd thing touching assault instruct admonyshe people mynd concerning comfort theym enterpryse called togither made oration wyse p euer beleueth good souldiours ye nowe brought hyther assault wynne one towne dothe consyder labour peyne therin profyte shall ensue therof trewe ye shall assault skale walles one onely towne obteynyng one ye also shall wynne whole cuntrey spayne towne pledge noble men kynges people spayne one taken full shortly shall cause euer carthaginenses doo nowe possede yelded vnto v vnder dominon also al money tresure ennemies whiche taken shall able longer maynteyne warres seinge haue many hyred straungers theyr army treasure shall meruaylously profyte v therby wynne hertes loue barbarous people besyde remaineth theyr ordinace armour al abilimentes necessary warre whiche beynge one wonne shall serue well pourpose therof make ennemies bare theyr vtter distruction furthermore shall lordes fayre ryche citie whervnto lyeth goodly hauen whereby shall serued sea lande thinges shall tyme lacke hauing thynges shal plesant profitable v also lacke shal muche greatter hyndrance losse ennemies citie hath theyr greattest strength theyr store house corne theyr treasaurye theyr armory theyr house stuffed thynges necessarye theyr shyppes warre generally citie onely receptacle haue hyther lyeth ryght course sea affrica spayn nowe sen perceyue ye sufficiently instructed haue thinges good ordre mete purpose lette v good hertes strength make haste assaultyng newe carthage p therwithall euery man loude voice assented therto thinkyng slacke busynes went furthe towarde carthage causing assauted water lande p syde mago capitain cartha ginenses perceiuing assault ordeined giuen sea land disposed men within towne maner two townesmen caused armed put aray part towne romain tetes campe fiue c men appoynted kepe castell v c assigned remayne vppon hylle within citie towarde easte rest people commanded redy helpe succour company place towne euer sawe nede resist whan euer herde crye made parte violent force assauting sodainly gate open wherat caused ii souldiours towne issue vpon romains whose fyrst coming scipio caused men recule backe thintent might draw towne nere reste romayne army fyrst battayle styf e well maynteined partes whan carthagineses per ceiued great numbre cominge tentes romains succour felowes fledde greate feare towarde citie chased slayne harde theyr gate caused lesse tremblyng citie battayle moche diuers place walles lefte bare naked without men defende euery man lept appoynted place great sodayne theyr feare perceiued well scipio standyng hyll without towne wherefore commaunded souldiours come tentes spedyly assaulte towne bring theim scalyng ladder commaundement fulfylled fyght strong bothe partes encourage people scipio hym selfe came thyther vnder couert shyldes pauesses withstande shotte came walles arowes dartes ingynnes whiche greate somtyme exhorted coumforted men somtime counsayled best attayning theyr purpose presence awytnesse bothe ofmens valyant courage also theyr cowardyse wherby euery man enforced hym selfe clymmevp neyther regardynge heyghte walles fearyng men armes fiersely defended walles syde towne lyke assault gyuen shyppes part laye towarde water small purpose mago furnyshed walles armed men euer bryngynge theym plenty dartes ordinance roman lost wane aboue al thinges sauing town height walles wherby fewe ladder able reche toppe ladder wer longest wer therto weake whan one ascended vp wolde also clyme theron heauy burden loded many brake great hurt climers whervpon scipio co sidering vaine labour caused wery company withdraw rest wherby carthagineses wer eased releued present feare danger also therby toke hardy courage opinion citie danger taking assault wer strong inough defend tyll capitaines carthaginenses army might haue time inough come rescous reise siege drewthen towarde middel day certain fysshermen tarracon ben fishing botes said great large poole lay northwest part towne certified scipio water therof low ebbe also northwind quicke driuing waues tide caused lower vale lightly great pole make romains passage open way neuer man passed stronge persuasion caused rest army rested tentes time first assault take ladder engine gyue newe assault place beaten back began fierse cruel warre hauinge sure hope naturall strengthe parte reason water made munimentes defence yet lefte watch euery man gone defence partes thassault semed fierse dangerouse without resistence entred towne incontinent made hast come gate battaile busy strong wha wer com found al townsman ernest defece coforting felowes neither herd saw roman tyl perceiued backes throwing dartes sleynge partes nother tyl time knewe town tha anon wer gate broken gret nu bre armed entred gate many time goten ouer walles som went incontinent towne sleyng met company wente araye market place myddel citie perceyued theyr ennemies fleyng hyl within towne kepte v c men warre mago great numbre fledde castel scipio sent parte host sayd hyll whiche anone wonne people slayne el taken rest wente assaulte castel whiche mago season valyantly defended seyng towne full ennemies lyke haue socours yelded vp selfe castell romaynes ceassed make slaughter citie euery man wente spoile towne praye whereof greate well golde syluer ordinaunce artyllary corne shyppes iron laten many thinges mete apparel shippes certayntie wherof wyll reherse writars vary moch therin also x prysoners taken wherof many citizen scipio let go libertie suffered dwel styl towne enioy moche goodes spoyled amonge prisoner two craftes men caused bod men worke common profytte citie rome puttyng comfort within shorte space made free wolde labour worke earnestely suche necessaryes shoulde haue nede warre greate noumber rest seruauntes lusty yonge men sent rower shyppes galeys place suche lacked also encreased nauy eyght shyppes wel furnished beside al prisoner also pledge noble men city greate noumbre whome caused well kepte gently entreated rest daye scipio gaue lycence wery men rest theym selues fewe al daye ben sore trauayled fyghtyng one place custody towne gaue cn lelius company see men selfe wente tentes p gentylnes scipio restoryng fayre yonge virgin vndefiled luceius vnto fyaunced cap xlvi morowe assembled hoste togyther fyrst gaue humble thankes praise goddis gyuen handes one day great noble riche citie lyke wherof found spain ennemies gathered togither treasure bothe affrica also spayne abundance lyttell nothyng left romayns hauyng great plenty thinges nexte muche praysed noble courage valyantnes men warre nother sodayne excursation theyr ennemies towne nother hygh walles water coulde make afrayde let theyr enterpryse nother yet theyr castels strong towres coulde resist theyr power aboue praised muche twayn first scaled walles entred towne eche gaue crowne good value souldiours rewarded euery man vertue merites specially cn lelius gouernour nauye praysed muche loued whome gaue rewarde crowne golde xxx ox p caused pledge brought willyng good comforte shuld consider wer power romayns whose naturall propretie desire bynde men throughe theyr benefytes shewinge loue rather compulsion kepe men feare leauer ioyne strange nation amitie faithfull felowshyp sorowfully kepe myserable seruitude toke name city pledge ambassadours chaunce hym present sayde city incontinent delyuered pledge vnto theim city sent messangers wyllynge theim send vnto theim shulde haue theyr pledge frely delyuered also taken many noble matrones honest maydens committed sobre honest men kept without force dishonour done vnto among captiues one virgin brought vnto hym excellent beautie euer went men delyted beholde scipio enquired cuntrey kynred descended perceyned betrouthed made sure yong prince celtiberias whose name luceius wherevppon incontinent sent said yonge man also parentes whose coming knowyng yonge man soore enamoured thus sayd vnto hym yonge man haue sente also yong man come cause whan yong maiden fianced ensured brought soldiors herd say entierly loued beautie witnesseth haue good cause might laufully enioy pleasaunt loue otherwyse occupied mynde affayres commune welthe coulde perchaunce beare loue desyre enioy nowe wyll beare fauour loue ryght ought haue hath bene well honourably kept virginite preserued though dwelled styl owne parentes thintent might make present acceptable conseruation mine honor gift require one reward hesforth becom louing fred roma ye esteme good honorable man father vncle reputed thinke noble citie rome many like vnto v trust neuer people daye founde earth wyll gladder haue loue frend shyppe ye wolde sory haue displeasure yong man gret thankes gyuen hym praide goddes rewarde goodnes power suffised parentes mayden called forthe broughte great summe golde redemption theyr chyld perceiued giuen frely husband desired take parte therof theyr gyfte declaration theyr good hertes towardes hym affirminge receyuinge therof shulde ioyfull vnto restitution theyr dowghter vndefiled p scipio beinge ouercome theyr longe vehement intercession caused sayde summe layde grounde fete callinge luceius againe hym sayde besyde dowere ye shal receyue father lawe mariage doughter ye shall also take gyfte dower hande whiche great gift also moch honour hym done besyde retourned home house countrey declaring euery man honour magnifycence scipio sayinge yonge man come lyke vnto god bothe power warre also gentilnesse liberalitie peace ouercome countrey yonge gentilman leauing house familye good ordre shortely retourned scipio bringynge hym cccc good horseman ayde socour romaynes p scipio sent c lelius rome beare tidynges victory hym sent mago xv senatours shirmishes hym ca xlvii estate warres spayne durynge whiche tyme consull marcellus toke salapia treason ii townes samnite force slewe iii men warre whiche anniball lefte kepyng townes cn fuluius proconsull trusting wynne herdonea anniball stronge selfe neither garnyson left sufficient defence therof remoued thyther army hauyng hope comfort atteyne knew wel annibal losse salapia departed cuntrey brutians suche sure frendes anniball towne herdonea sent hym priuyly worde messangers desyrous kepe styl old frendes hasted horseman lyghtest footemen makyng great iourneys alredy com nere herdonea fame comig wer well knowen put romayns feare appered good aray battaile sodainly baners displaied whiche fuluius perceiuynge lyke hardynes made spede put folke aray ioyned battayle hym anniball comanded horseman signe token theim made while romains busy battail footemen euery man eye wer occupied busyly shoulde secretelye cooste fielde parte set vpon backes ennemies one parte inuade campe tentes greate noyse slaughter saying trusted vanquyshe fuluius ii yeres paste ouercome fuluius name cuntrey hope nothing deceyued soone horseman assailed romayns theyr backes great feare slaughter anon campe hearde great crye wherby romayns kept aray fought boldly disinayd fledde many mo slayne among said fuluius xii tribune xiii romayns slayne theyr campe stuffe taken p anniball trustyng nothyng strengthe towne remoued inhabitantes therof metapontus thurines slew capitains therof secrete comunication consull set town fyre p marcellus consulle baynge nothynge afrayde tydinges losse sente letter senate rome byddynge whytte discomforted therwith doubted wolde cause anniball haue short ioy victory whervpo immediately remoued toward annibal pitchyng campe playne fieldes euen syght ennemies soone valyantly came furthe order battayle redy fyght syde anniball lesse quicke battayle betwene bothe horseman footemen meruaylous fiers cruell neither ceassed tyll nyght departed indifferet losse party night anniball secretly remoued went apulia marcellus mornyng perceyuynge departure ennemies folowed incontinent ouertoke theim nere vnto venusia thus passed apulia without notable battaile one folowinge euer anniball wolde remoue nyght sekyng place deceiue ennemies consull always folowed day tyme sendynge hym espies sure crafty trayne anniball p summer almost ended tyme chosynge consul drewe nere whiche chusyng marcellus shulde haue hym selfe sent letter rome affyrmynge shulde ryght hurtfull common welth yf dyd depart one foote anniball absence yea onely ceassyng assayle hym shulde gyue hym moche courage whervpon comaunded abyde stylle army consul liuius sent chosen consul q fabius maximus q fuluius flaccus besyde determined claudius marcellus shulde kepe also army warres agaynst anniball one yere longar p touchynge warres spayne ordeyned publius scipio sullanus shoulde gouernours onely yere vnto tyme called senate p aboute tyme came ambassadours kynge syphax affrica rome shewynge prosperous battayles hadde fought carthaginenses desyrynge haue amitie romaynes agreed hym whole senate whyche moued betwene hym two bretherne cneius p scipio spayne whose ambassadours senatours gaue gentyl thankes louynge answeres also sent kyng ryche presentes p longe tidinges wer brought rome affrica massanissa sonne kynge gala come carthage v numidian great numbre affricans wer hyred go ouer spayne asdruball intent strongly accompanied might depart shortly then italy brother annibal iudged hope theyr victory rest p time came lelius spayne rome bryngynge hym great numbre prisoner rehersynge senate house happy wynnynge newe carthage one daye gettyng many newe friendes spaine newes made theim mery comming asdruball italy made theim afrayde consyderinge come theyr power skant able resiste onely power anniball neuerthelesse good chere coulde discharged lelius sendyng hym agayne spayne shyppes came hym p marcellus gyueth battayle anniball whiche men put flyght wherupon maketh sharpe oration reneweth battayll morowe putt th anniball host flight losse many men cap xlviii newe consull leauynge thynges good order rome departed towardes warres q fuluius flaccus passed capua whome q fabius made instant requeste departed wolde kepe strayght quicke warres anniball whyles dyd besiege citie tarent whiche citie myghte one take frome hym shulde haue place sure go neyther knowe cost myght safely tourne hym shuld afterwarde haue small cause abide italy request also made marcellus letter thynkynge man italy able matche anniball hym selfe kendeled stirred fabius letter sone wynter passed fode founde fieldes able susteyne army cattel went canusium annibal laye hadde moued ruler towne yelde vnto hym leauyng romayne amitie sone parceyued marcellus come remoued thense leauynge playne countrey sought hylly woddy countrey whiche myght apte traynes deceipte ennemies p marcellus euer folowed harde ioyning almost campe campe dyuers skyrmyshes made betwene horse men bothe partes anniball mynding ieoparde one fledde hym nyghte last ouertoke hym playne fielde anniball caused campe trenched fortified marcellus men let workes therof whether wold enforced batayl thyng eschued wherefore ordered theyr army bothe party fought tyll nyght departed morowe marcellus early put men good aray anniball dydde exhortyng men remembre noble conquestes trasymenus canna suffre theyr gredye vnreasonable ennemy vexe might haue tyme incampe selues ye scarsely loke aboute take breathe sonne whan ryseth romain army bothe one tyme appere fieldes case saythe ye handle hym may one departe losse men fielde wil herafter easy intreate exhortation also euyl contented tedious continuall pursuing theyr enemy fiersly went battaile fought cruelly space ii longe houres last ryght wynge romayns gaue backe whose place fulfyll marcellus appoynted legion men armes company fyrst reculed feare came fayntly place last romayn host fearefull shamefast began flee slayn day romains ii thousand seuen hundred wherof iiii wer capitaines hundreders two tribune p marcellus come campe made souldiours soore cruell oration wordes angry capitayne semed displeasaunt peynefull trauayle toke battaylle daie p moche bounde sayth immortall goddes ye fearfully toumbled together tentes chaunced ennemy victory assayle campe also fayle loke feare ye left battayle lyke feare also ye forsaken campe sodayne feare hath nowe inuaded thynge hath caused sone forget bothe estate selfe also ennemies ye remembre ennemies ye ouercame pursued last somer whome fleinge bothe daye night ye chased cutreis ye yesterday ye wold neither suffer flee yet gyue theim moche time fortifye theyr fielde wil reherse thynges wherein ye may glory nowe wyll declare thynges whereof ye ought moche ashamed yester daye ye departed batayle euen hande nowe hath daye nyghte ben greate lette vnto taken army therby whit lessed theyr power whyt encreased truely thinketh nowe speake mine owne company souldiours yet romains perceiue nothing theim body armour ye hertes mides ennemies shuld neuer haue loked backes loste none standardes time could neuer glorie slaughter company yesterdaie ye gaue honour death felowes p euerie man cried aloude desirynge pardon daie past one againe trie herte courage men euer shulde please nowe saide truely wyl proue againe wil morowe morninge set forthe araie intent ye vanquisher may aske forgiuenes rather people vanquished p morrowe men well eaten dronken made theim stronge put people order set v warde fled first daye company loste standardes best lyked comaundinge theim earnestely fyghte ouercome theyr ennemies victorie present daie might fly come rome sclaunder yesterday flienge p whan anniball herd fierse courage marcellus sayd haue nowe suche ennemye neyther suffre good fortune badde yf ouercom ennemies gredily styl assaileth theim whan ouercome also fiersly renueth warres vpon theim wordes incontinent brought hoste furthe fielde battayle cruell daie carthaginenses euer stryuynge kepe honour romaynes auenge shame gotten daie aduauntage battayle betweene theim abode longe suspence marcellus present witnesse euer redye comforte exhorte romayn anniball seinge doubtefulnesse fyght victory putte ennemies sodayne feare caused elephantes sette agaynste forewarde whyche fyrste comynge brought theim order didde theim muche trouble hurte wherby one parte thereof lefte bare voyde resystence reste fled also hadde decius flauius tribune taken standerde one bandes horseman commaundynge company belongynge standerde folowe hym boldely obeyde incontinent brought theim company elephantes dyd moste displeasure causynge mooste trouble rumour badde theim couragiousely throwe theyr dartes speares beastes whyche dyd woundynge many theim feelynge theim selues hurt greatte rage runne away coulde stayed theim rode theim romaynes folowed theim styll droue thiem vpon theyr owne company spanyardes carthaginenses makynge greatter slaughter amonge theim hadde done romaynes whan sawe carthaginenses meane brought array romaine footemen order entred brake aray cleane puttynge theym flyght marcellus caused horsmen folow chase ceassed tyl wer driuen yates campe great losse bothe men elephantes slayne daye viii men fyue elephantes romaine slayne thre thousande many sore hurt whervpon annibal next nyght folowinge remoued vnto brutians marcellus abode season cure hurt souldiours p home q fabius maximus recouered anniball citie tarent cap xlix season q fabius max consul toke manduria force then remoued tarent pytchyng tentes hardeby mouth hauen founde certayne shyppes whyche liuius late consull hadde left defence shyppes brought vytayle necessary prouision castell shyppes also came vitayles prouision thyther charged gunnes stone kynde weapon inuasiue somme laded scalyng ladder engyns assaulte towne soo sea al thinges wer ready assaulte land also ordered copany help purpose acheued ther chaunced small thing estimation yet proued meruailous happy successe great enterprise anniball sent tarent crue men warre countrey brutians capytayne company meruailously enamored yong woma citie whose brother souldiour host fabius sister sent worde letter familiaritie new acquaintaunce earnest louer greate ryches honour whervpon man imaginynge trustyng also loue syster myght leade louer euer wolde diuise conceyued hope good therby touchynge wynnynge towne whervpon secretely opened mynde capitayne fabius desyrynge hym woulde ly ence hym departe frome armye goo citie whiche woulde vndertake dooe dissemblynge hym selfe stolen away company loue sister desyrouse cytezen consull thynkyng proue effecte opynyon suffered hym departe thus came syster meanes felle greate familiarite louer capytayne brutianes longe acquayntaunce beganne couertly proue mynde lyttell lyttell whan founde towardnesse hym sette syster hande hym fayre flatterynge woordes soo compassed hym haue loue consented betraiynge parte citie wher rular capytayne p whan agreed tyme maner circumstaunce purpose souldyour secretly nyghte lette furthe towne came capitayn declarynge vnto hym hadde doone waye shoulde take achieue enterpryse tyme houre appoynted whiche begynnynge nyght consull hadde prepared sea syde hauen shyppes menne warre thereto appoynted shoulde vyolentely assaulte towne parte romaynes castell theyr force also shulde assayle citizen good numbre hym pryuyly drewe hym easte parte towne abode longe season withoute makynge noyse greatte noyse bruite made purposely hauen syde syde towardes castelle leaste daungier soo democrates capytayne whyche nyghe vnto crew brutians fearynge leste absence romaynes myghte chaunce syde wynne towne whyche feare moued greatte rumour crye cytezens parte whan hearde thynges quiete reste parte towne wherin people hasted towarde castell syde hearde greattest noyse p consull heringe thenoyse ceassed men armes whiche loude iudging kepers warde gone then commanded streight scalynge ladder sette walles syde brutians kepte warde whyche done without resystence brutians onely made noo resystence alsoo holpe theym vp thus entred towne streyghte wente nexte gate whyche brake caused moche theyr companye entre theyr baners dysplayed breake day came markette place tarentines parceyuinge theyr towne taken came theyr power frome castell side hauen succour therof late battayle lyttell begonne felte selues farre vnable resist romaynes wherfore anon fled euery man house friendes house wer nico democrates slayne battayle philomenes chiefe autour betraying towne anniball toke horse fledde whither wente became hym knowen great slaughter made carthaginenses tarentines many prisoner taken ryche spoyle wall whiche anniball made deuyde castell frome towne throwen downe p anniball fyrste hearde tarent besieged hast possible hyed thyther succour therof came nere thervnto hearde newes takynge citie meanes sayde nowe ryght well fynde romaynes haue also anniball amonge theim euen suche crafte wanne tarent suche haue lost shulde appeere reculed feare pitched campe fyue mile citie taryed certayne dayes thense went metapontus caused letter written two chiefe ruler citie fabius contentes therof woulde please romaynes hym receyue theim theyr grace remitte theyr olde iniuries wronges doone woulde delyuer handes bothe towne also garnison carthaginenses wer within fabius nothynge mistrustinge sent agayne appoyntynge tyme wolde come metapontus speake whiche letter streyght brough anniball beinge ioyouse trayne deceyue old wise fabius tyme appoynted layde great embusshemente vpon waye fabius shulde passe metapontus p tyme fabius shulde departe sought diuinations augury howe shulde spede voiage kyllyng beaste therwith sacrifyce lucke byrdes detestable vse longe ben amonge romaynes whiche augury vnlucky vntowarde shewed hym euyll aduenture wente forwarde appoynted iourney wherfore deuynours wyse men aduysed hym tary styll tentes feare treason p metapontans seing fabius came day assigned sent agayne hym requyring hym come capitaynes whiche messangers incontinente taken examyned vpon case fearynge tourmentes wer prepared theim confessed deceyte treson wherby fabius escaped death destruction many armye p scipio fyghteth hasdruball besyde betula dryueth hym hyll sleith viii host taketh xii prysoners massus neuew massanissa great praye campe cap l summer tyme whyles thynges done italy p scipio beinge spayne gotten loue spanyardes edisco indibilis mandonius thre great prince spayne come amitie alliaunce indibilis desired commynge myght dishonorable vnto man shulde reproche theim stolen awaye theyr olde friendes carthage lyke lyght people runne romaynes sayde doone worthely tymes whiche theyr kyndenesse euer recompensed pryde auaryce many iniuries onely theyr bodyes abode amitie carthage theyr hertes hadde longe beene towardes romaynes knewe euer kepers theyr truse taken mainteinours right equitie wherfore desyred scipio receyue theyr friendely commynge vnto hym accordynge theyr meanynge intente founde dylygent theyr seruyce doynge vnto esteme scipio hertely thanked grauntynge theyr requestes thynges wheruppon theyr wyues chyldren restored vnto theim whiche captyues scipio stedfaste aliaunce amitie knytte betwene theim sone theyr hole power men war came prynces ioyned campe romaynes departinge guided euer tyl brought nere campe theyr ennemies p meane armye greatly increaced yet besydes one waye scipio polytikely augmented host sawe nauy car hage sea neded haue great noumbre men shyppes broughte hoole nauye tarracon takynge souldiours whiche theim alsoo parte maryners hym warres lande great hooste wente forwardes made suche spede secretly came nere vnto towne betula hasdruball laye armye theyr fyrste commynge thyther certeyne smalle skyrmysshes made betwene theim hasdruball seynge romaynes power dayly increased made lesse thoughte woulde ieoparde fyghte without lenger prolongynge tyme determyned seeke place strengthe myght fyghte aduauntage hurte ennemyes wherfore nyghte remoued armye hyghe hyll nere adioynynge toppe wherof fayre large playne backe syde hyll ranne ryuer whiche compassed good parte hyll furthermore aboute myddes hyll another playne fyelde moche lower playne vnto nether playne ascendyng hard peinfull lower fyelde asd uball day folowyng sent great numbre numidian horseman light harnessed fotemen affrica iles called baleares nowe named maiorque minorque p scipio rydynge aboute hoste shewed theim theyr ennemyes theyr hertes saythe wyll serue theym fyghte v euen grounde wherfore seeke hyghe mountaynes trustynge strengthe place theyr owne strengthe armour newe carthage hadde hye walles whiche neuerthelesse scaled romayne souldyours neyther coulde hyghehylles castell thereof yet sea withstande theyr power knowe saythe hye place whiche ennemyes haue chosen thynke shall serue theym flye v leapynge runnyng downe stiepenesse therof wayes wyll also stoppe frome theim wherevpon incontinente scipio sente two company menne warre commaundynge one kepe mouthe valley whiche ryuer ranne shulde abyde secretely waye laye bowinge mountayne betwene towne betula fyeldes hym selfe good noumbre nymble harnessed men wente streyghte towardes numidian affricanes whiche lower playne hyll whoo suffered theim come almooste vppe withoute let saue onely styepenesse hylle vntyll came within castynge dartes thenne fyghte soore bothe partes specially great plenty stoones inginnes throwen hyll romaine neuerthelesse althoughe hylle verye tediouse harde wonne also almooste ouerwhelmed stone yet beinge nymble well harted men moche vsed approchynge scalynge walles ceassed goo styll vppewarde tyll formooste theym hadde gotten playne euen grounde anone putte numidyans flyghte greatte slaughter droue theym vppe theyr armye abode hygheste parte hyll thenne scipio commaunded companye go streyghte vppe towarde myddle theyr ennemyes rest hoste deuyded two partes wherof caused lelius take one halfe go aboute ryght hande hyll espy myghte fynde easye place ascende parte kept lefte hande ere euer fette farre compasse clambe vp sayde mountayne ran ennemyes whose backes wer toward wherwith host carthaginenses sore troubled great clamour made inforcynge tourne resyst scipio company chaunge theyr ordre whiche troublous bruite came lelius theym side whose coming caused foreward gyue backe feare inuaded behynde meane wherof myddell warde scipio gotte hylle whyche possible theim haue wonne army elephantes kepyng aray place stiepe ascend began carthaginenses flee sauegard great slaughter made among abode scipio company fledde many receyued ii company layde embusshement purpose slayne numbre viii men asdruball seing beginning battaile nothing prosperous intent sent money many elephantes away folowed many coulde saue selues flieng passyng ryuer tagus went streight toward mountain pyreneis p scipio comynge campe carthaginenses gaue pray therof souldiours except prisoner wer numbre x thousand fotemen ii horseman whiche numbre soo many spanyardes let go lybertie freely without raunsome paying rest caused sold questor gaue large gyftes princis spayn specially indibilis gaue iii c horse beste coulde chuse taken whiche liberall distribution commune spayne called hym kyng whyche name scipio declared odious detestable roman wherfore desyred absteyne callyng hym name name gouernour capitayne well contented p whan questor sell prysoners capitaynes commaundement among found goodly yonge chylde xv yeres olde whome sente scipio herd descended lignage roial scipio enquired countrey greatter age happened campe amonge men warre aunswered numidia named massus father sayd deade wherfore mother sent father sala kinge numidia frome time ben brought vp vncle massanissa vncle came ouer spaine socour carthaginenses came also euer went batteil vncle wolde suffer hym go time sayde neuer came fyelde nowe also vnware sayde vncle euery man made hym redye pryuely also toke horse harneies entered battayle chaunce euyll nowe faule horse wherby taken romaynes scipio demaunded hym whether desyrous retourne massanissa aunswered wepynge ioye wolde verye glad chaunce good scipio gaue ringe golde cote senatours garmente spanysshe cloke goodly horse well harneysed buckle golde suffered hym departe vncle pleasure appoyntynge horsemenne conducte hym waye farre woulde haue theim p thynges done bestowed reste summer receyuynge many people city spayne amitie romaynes remayned tarracon p sone battayle foughte betula asdruball sonne gysgon mago theyr armyes came frome parte spayne helpe asdruball late battayle paste theyr comynge wherfore consulted beste doone laste consyderynge scipio gyftes lyberalytye hadde hertes hyther partes spayne onely people furtheste parte co ntreye towardes gades pyllers hercules knewe yet nothynge hym romaynes wherfore sure frendes carthaginenses determyned necessytie muste remoue theyr souldiours spayne eyther furtheste partes spayne elles fraunce elles shorte space woulde turne frendship romaynes p also agreed asdruball takynge hym al spanyardes spayne farre name scipio shulde go ouer mountaynes towardes anniball italy heade chiefe grounde warres p furthermore mago leauinge host asdruball sonne gysgon shuld passe ouer sea iles called baleares nowe called maiorque minorque great summe money shulde also hire many mo souldiours theyr helpe purpose whose departyng asdruball sonne gysgon host appointed depart portugall shoulde wyse fyght romayns massanissa iii best lightest horse men appoynted hym whiche numbre assigned pervse ryde abrode countreys helping city frendes carthaginenses spoile distroy townes fieldes ennemies intentes myndes euery one capitaines departed makyng greate spede achieue enterpryse p marcellus consull slayn imbushement layde anniball crispinus consull marcellus sonne soore hurte capi li fame scipio dayly encreased rome also q fabius maximus gotten greate honour wynnynge towne tarent marcellus meane ennemies runne great infamy reported anniball rouyng abrode countrey kept host sommer season towne venusia marcellus purge hym sclaunderous name came rome againste tyme chusynge offycers thyther came alsoo q fuluius flaccus consull cause marcellus openly debated c bibulus one tribune charged hym soore sayeng negligence marcellus suche lyke cause anniballes longe abode italy sayd tenthe yere sen came fyrst countrey hath lyued almost long italy hath done carthage chosyng officer ye wylled claudius marcellus continue yere longar office nowe ye wyll knowe fruite hath brought forth yere meane therof ye shall vnderstande hath hooste two tymes beaten many slayne yere chiefe sommer hath kepte resydue men venusia within sure walles p accusation marcellus wysely sobrely aunswered shewynge policy actes doone agaynste anniball excuse onely welle taken also well dooinge daye folowynge hole consent people chosen consull titus quintus crispinus chosen felowe appoynted kepe italy agaynste anniball marcellus wente olde army venusia takyng hym dyuers supplye place slayne crispinus seinge honour growen fabius wynnyng tarent thoughte besyege citie locrus wherfore sent maner ordynances sicilia shyppes also assault sea well land hearinge cominge anniball lacinium lefte pourpose season ioyned hoste fellowe marcellus come venusia countrey apulia bothe incamped army iii myles one frome thyther came also anniball soone parceyued consull crispinus hadde lefte besiegynge locrenses cuntrey pytched campe tentes yere assayed power herte marcellus sometyme wynnyng sometyme losse men wherefore fearynge power bothe consulles ouermatched diuysed howe policy craft deceiue consulles made dyuers skyrmyshes men thinkyng suche tryflynge frayes passe furthe sommer kepe hym occupied yet neuerthelesse trusted stronge ynough also besiegynge locrus wherfore sent sicilia causyng l cincius nauy army come besiegynge locrus sea furthermore assayle also lande commaunded part army whiche laye defence tarent brought thyther appoyntement pryuyly done anniball hadde knowledge therof certayne thurines whervppon agaynste tyme appoynted theyr comynge sent embusshement two thousande horseman thre thousande footemen lye secretely vnder hylle petillia vppon way wherby romayne tarentines shoulde passe romaynes vnaduysedly passyng waye amonge great hurtes two thousande theim slayne one two hundred taken prysoners rest escaped fledde dyuers way backe agayne tarent consulles laye theyr seuerall campes farre frome campe anniball nowe myddell waye betwene romaynes campe hym greatte hylle full woodde taken viewed romayns feared viewe doubted maner grounde vttermooste parte thereof towarde theyr enemy neither viewed anniball estemed place mete deceiue ennemies pytche theron campe wherefore nyght sent thither company numidian horseman lye pryuily myddell wood without mouynge makynge noyse daie tyme feare espied romaynes euer cryed theyr capytaynes shoulde take sayde hylle pytche one theyr campes feare leste anniball shoulde take theim said marcellus felowe crispinus lette v certaine horseman v go viewe hyll yghte whereof maye dispose thynges accordyngly beynge thus agreed takyng ii hundred xx horseman wente bothe suruey sayde hylle wood yonge marcellus consul sonne aulus manlius beinge bothe tribune folowed couetous mynde marcellus ioyne battaile anniball thoughte coulde neuer ioyne campe nyghe ynough campe ennemye wherefore departynge caused people redynesse case place lyked theim myghte gather vp vesselles theyr stuffe folowe theim frome theyr campes p capytaynes passed thorough lyttell playne fielde frome thense entred fayre brode waye rydynge whyche wente vp woodes toppe rydynge numidian hadde sette espy watche thynkynge soo greate praye happed theim come onely watche forrageours wood caryars shoulde happe roue abrode vytayles wood suche necessary espye warned theym romaynes commynge numbre gaue theim sygne whan euery man theim shoulde leape oute secrete denne whyche craftyly executed gaue theym sygne issue oute tyll romaynes soo farre passed theyr wa e hyndermoste parte embusshement myght inclose theim stoppe theyr waye behynde theim tyme formoste embushement assayled theim partes issued layde romaynes consulles seynge theim selues stopped bothe behynde foughte manfullye theym selues comforted theyr fellowes thynkynge prolonge battayle tylle succour myghte come soo fierse parte romaynes fledde neuer lesse reste foughte season tylle sawe crispinus soore wounded felowe marcellus thruste thorough speare falle deade grounde thanne reste left lyue fledde crispinus consull soore hurte two dartes yonge marcellus beynge also soore wounded aulus manlius slayne marcus aulius foure forty horseman arenius fyue sergeantes consulles eyghtene horseman taken prisoner p anniball craftily sendeth lettters salapia sealed marcellus sygnet asdruball passeth mountayns army mete brother anniball cap lii anniball knowynge greatte feare woulde romayne hooste deathe one consulle also woundynge putte theym feare incontynent remoued hooste hylle battayle hadde beene pytched campe founde bodye marcellus whiche caused buryed crispinus beinge sore feared deathe fellowe also owne woundes nyght folowynge remoued secretelye armye highest nexte hyll suertie coulde fynde pitchinge campe tentes capitaines endeuoured selues vttermost one deceyue eschewe deceite p anniball bodye marcellus founde alsoo ringe sygnet wherby trusted worke deceytfull conclusion crispinus mystrustinge also sente spede worde city romaynes nere adioyninge warnynge theim felowe marcellus slayne anniball gotten signet wherfore commanded theim wyse gyue credence letter shulde sente vnto sealed seale marcellus made name soone messanger came salapia anniball letter written sealed name marcellus shewynge vnto nyght folowynge marcellus wolde priuely come thyther wherfore commaunded capitaynes garrison redy commynge knowe pleasure done salapiens fyndynge crafte wrytynge sente backe messangers anniball gentyll answere nyghte prefyxed sette sure watche warde walles specially parte towne gate demed theyr ennemyes wolde come lyttell daye came anniball great company hym first company cam yates roman wer departed cuntrey taken wage anniball romayne armour came gate spake laten dydde romaynes wakynge watchemen byddynge open gate consull watche arose great leuers lyft vp port colyes soo hyghe men myghte entre vnder sayde bande romaynes runawayes entered fast myght entred numbre vi c rope whiche dyd holde vp portcolyes let slyp fell downe great noyse makynge salapiens smalle resystence slewe entred towne mystrustinge suche thyng bare harneys hanginge theyr shulders thynkyng haue entred peace many towne speares dartes chased theyr ennemyes gate walles p thus anniball beinge taken owne trappe deceyued thense departed rayse syege friendes locrenus cincius souldiours ordynaunce came sicilia kept harde strayghte p mago citie herynge death marcellus toke comforte vnto hym harde tydynges anniball sente numidian horseman coming hym selfe fotemen spedely myght withoute feare wherfore espyed afarre numidian approchyng caused gate opened arraye folke issued vpon romaynes sodeyne comyng strengthe caused battayle endure season doubtefull numidian also come romaynes stryken feare withoute ordre ranne towarde theyr shyppes leauynge behynde theym theyr ordynaunce wherwith beaten walles meane syege locrensis raysed p crispinus consull sente letter rome bothe felowes deathe also sore hurtes letted could come rome chosyng consul senatours pensyfe se two consul army destitute capitaynes wherfore day election loked fynd two wisd circumspect person offyce ben acqueynted deceites anniball fyrste aboue lyked c claudius nero knewe valyaunt man good capytayne estemed hym quicke tyme warres matche soobre capytayne anniball wherfore deuysed match quickenes sobre felowe great temperance one liuius man great sobrenesse late come agayne citie ben consull viii yeres passed consulshyppe condempned comons without fault put offyce shame hym done toke displeasauntly leauynge citie wente forthe countrey dwell company men viii yeres condempnation marcellus valerius leuinus consulles brought hym home agayne citie founde hym foule euyll apparellyd heare bearde longe token shame receiued time censor caused hym rounde heare puttynge cleane garmentes come senate house brought thyther father examyned theyr opinion liuius touchyng offyce consull agreed senatours common mete couple hym claudius nero alone refused office accusyng citezens vnkynde lyghtnesse sayinge p meruayle moche ye laye nowe burthen office ye late thruste oute offyce thynkyng vnworthy therof ye accompt good honeste man dyd ye condempne euyll man offender syns ye iudged euill gouerned consulshyp wherin laste truste ye nowe agayne roume p wordes accused father also common senatours rebuked hym wordes shewinge example furius camillus though banyshed citie rome yet restored agayne sayd lyke childe ought suffer sharpe punishement father ought euery man suffer punishement countrey pacience gentilnes p wordes appeased hym caused hym take hym sayde office p one consull appoynted kepe warre againste anniball italy leste shulde drawe nere asdruball cominge mountaynes succour assygned mete asdruball fame whome beganne approche mountaynes thintent come ouer ioyne power brother anniball opynion anniball dyd also mo helpe romaynes purpose althoughe knewe brother woulde sommer passe mountaynes come ouer hym yet whan remembred manyfold lettes selfe passynge ryuer rhodanus dangerus mountaynes stryuinge bothe men peryllous place wherin spent fyue monethes loked spedye quicke coming brother whiche caused hym long er euer remoued fro place wintred army moche deceiued asdruball better spede passage loked selfe frenchemen also mountaynoys dyd onely receiue suffered hym army passe countreys also folowed warres leadinge many sure wayes whiche anniball brother vnable passed agayne wayes ouer mountaynes continuall vse goinge ouer made moche easy people gentyll intreate annibals comynge vsed company straungers neyther sene countrey wherfore wylde sauage people thoughte also fyrste tyme carthaginenses come take theyr castelles cattell nowe fame warre holden italy betwene romaynes carthaginenses taught made know hole contention betwen noble head city worlde beinge farre distant sundre onely honour rich wolde trye whether shulde possede dominion hole p cause knowen made mountaynes open easy asdruball passe speede good passynge let great besieginge placentia whan come ouer thought citie beinge faire plaine countrey ben easy wynne fame wynnynge therof thoughte city adioyninge shulde haue trembled feare strength therof moche deceyued knewe anniball full wel came ouer riuer trebia vayne assayed strength therof asdrubals assieginge placentia onely lette owne iourneye also stayed anniball moche longer harde therof ere euer sette forthe place wyntered hoste p consulles theyr armyes went prouinces liuius towardes placentia whome ere departed q fabius warned exhorted shulde ouer hastyly fyght ennemies knewe maners condition theim liuius remaynynge yet dyspleasure towarde citezens banyshement answered wolde fyght theim soone might haue fyght whan cause demaunded hym wolde make therm suche haste truely sayd eyther wyll quyckely haue great honour subduinge myne ennemyes el greatte ioye sleynge myne owne vnkynde cytezens whyche ioye althoughe honeste yet shall accordyng theyr deseruynges p quintus claudius nero made haste tyll approched nere vnto anniball gone countrey lucanes lay towne grument claudius hadde army forty thousande fotemen two thousand fyue hundred horseman anniball gatherynge togyther moche power coulde amonge brutians suche fortress helde lay inc mped nigh vnto walles grument within halfe myle campe romaynes betwene bothe campes goodly playne valey hauynge oone syde fayre playne hylles without wooddes couerte hyde embusshement cause deceyte wherfore lesse suspecte bothe party hylles laye adioynyng lefte syde carthaginenses ryghte syde romaynes playne medowe many lyght eskyrmysshes made betweene hostes many excursyons romayne consull caused made onely kepe ennemyes frome goynge towarde asdruball p syde anniball desyrous remoue place power intended gyue hym battaile wherfore putte whole hoste array claudius nero perceyuynge intent caused secretely nyght folowynge titus assellus p claudius two tribune good noumbre men theim passe ouer sayde hylle adioynynge abyde valeye behynde hylles appoyntynge theim tyme whan shoulde descende mountayne backe theyr ennemies hym selfe breake daye reste footemen horseman came fielde good araye anniball lykewyse commaunded men arme theim greate noyse made campe euery man runnynge harneys whan armed ranne oute campe yates bothe horseman footemen without array anniball knowledge therof soone campe playne ranne ennemyes fyghtynge bothe horsebacke foote chaunce gaue theym meete theyr ennemies kepynge none order p whan consull sawe theym thus rounnynge abrode fyelde without order commaunded c arunculeus horseman legyon inuade carthaginenses moche vyolence myght wherby myght slea theym beinge without order lyke beastes coulde brought array whyche dydde dilygentely execute makynge greate slaughter battayle strong season reason contynuall resorte freshe souldiours runnyng succour theyr felowes p anniball yet campe hearyng noyse men fyghtyng came furthe reste power dilygently applyed selfe euen menne fyghtynge put many theym araye whiche thynge hath bene lyghtly seene therein shewed hym selfe experte capytayne hauyng olde well acquaynted warryours vnder hym thus brought wholle hoste order styll fyghtyng c assellus bandes romaynes sodainely descended hylles backe carthaginenses greate clamour meanes wherof beyng aferde lest shuld stopped campe began flee partes horseman slewe many chase many mo slayne campe nere hande yet lost anniball men battayle viii slayne vii c taken aliue next day diuers day romains array kept fielde desyrous fight carthaginenses abode styll theyr tentes p soone nyght anniball army remoued towardes apulia makinge great fyres campe towardes romaynes leauynge entree campe certayne numydian horseman shewe tyl hooste myght farre gone frome ennemyes whan day lyght sayd numidian shewed theim selues gate campe season purposely deceyue romaine whan sawe theyr tyme spedily rode theyr companie p consull hearynge noo noyse tentes ennemyes sent two light horsmen viewe theyr campe fyndynge voyde theyr ennemies retourned claudius certifiynge hym theyr departyng whervpon hoste wente thyther toke spoyle suche baggage leste morowe early folowed carthaginenses fame hearde waie whiche gone anniball willynge fyght toke waie euer nyght ouer mountaynes tyl came metapontus toke hanno soudiours whyche lefte ioyned theim armye sendynge hym smalle numbre hym countrey brutians assemble moo men warre succour p great battayle betwene asdruball consulles whyche asdruball slayne syx fyfty thousand men besyde many taken great spoyle cap liiii asdruball leauing assiegyng placentia sent foure frenchemen two numidian brother anniball letter passyng italy heryng anniball shoulde metapontus folowed thither er ware lost way came fieldes tarent taken sent claudius nero letter whan redde knewe contentes therof asdruball intended mete brother vmbria thynkyng tyme mete common welth tary determination senate imagyned would enterpryse strange thing wherby shulde put citezens rome also ennemies great feare lengthe whan achieued shulde tourne wholle citie greate feare meruailous gladnesse wherfore sent sayde letter rome owne letter intended enterpryse incontinent sente messangers hym townes countreys whych army shoulde passe commaundyng theim brynge furthe fieldes agaynst commynge vitayles horse necessary souldyours wholle armye chose vi thousande footemen one horsmen sayinge publyshyng intended assault next towne lucans take carthaginenses whiche left keping therof company nyght departed makyng great haste myghte iourney come healpe felowe liuius shulde haue asdruball leauynge quintus tatius campe rule gouerne rest hoste rome consulles letter made men lesse aferde two yeres past whan carthaginenses hadde pytched theyr tentes walles rome doubted whether myght allowe disallowe bolde enterpryse consull whyche dyd appere hange vpon chaunce knewe campe left nere anniball army dispurueyed capitayne ye flowre strengthe armye taken awaye capytayne leauynge campe sure nothynge onely ignoraunce ennemies priuy consulles absence yf happed knowen chaunced anniball wholle army folowe nero hauyng vi thousand fotemen armed one horseman wold assaile reste left campe without strength good gouernance euil chance susteined warres late dethe ii consul one yere increased feare whyche happed theim whan one capytayne one army ennemies italy nowe knewe ii myghty army ii valyant capitaines ye almost ii anniballes countrey asdruball sonne also amilcar hadde many yeres spayne made warre agaynste romayns hadde two noble victory sleynge two greate army also ii scipions noble capitayns furthermore myghte glory aboue anniball bothe spedy passage ouer mountaynes also drawyng hym frenchemen battayle euen one almoste loste greatter parte menne hungre colde whiche two greattest myseries warre euen gathered together gret puissance rekened also claudius nero shuld haue witty capitayn knewe mocked illuded hym spayne lyke child deceiteful intretyng condition peace wherby escaped straytes wherein indaungered thus throughe feare whiche thinterpretour thynges worste estemed power theyr ennemyes great owne small p meane tyme nero consull farre traueyled frome daunger ennemies iudged myght safely discouer secrete enterprise called together souldiours spake vnto sayinge neuer enterpryse taken hande capitayne whiche apparence bolde effect sure wyll nowe brynge sayde certayne sure victorye goo battayle whiche felowe liuius many fotemenne horseman appoynted hym senate wolde desyre ye suche numbre wolde haue desyred greatter shulde haue ben appoynted fyght anniball hym selfe nowe fame comynge consull armye beinge ioyned shall fayle haue vndoubted victory fame thynge gyueth victory battayle yea small thinges oft tymes driue hertes myndes men eyther feare good hope hole glorye honour good spede shall gyuen v euer whiche cometh last draweth honour p comforte led forward theyr way passynge great multitude men woman countrey came forth mete great fauour prayse giuynge namynge patron defendours co mon welthe hole empyre rome whose handes laye helthe welth lybertie bothe theyr child wherfore prayed vnto apulia also present hand shalbe deceyued thynkynge numbre lesse thinking numbre nothynge increased p earnest wordes claudius departed fro counsaile euery man armed hym selfe put good order battayle carthaginenses also alredy come theyr campe stode array redy fyght bothe army without taryeng gone gither asdrubal season caused company stay certayne horseman company rode host perceiued amonges romaynes many olde shildes whiche seene also marked many carreine leane ouer laboured horse thought also numbre ennemies greatter wont wherfore hauyng mistrust whiche dede true blewe retraite incontinent sent certayn men ryuer romayne horse watered espye marke whether theyr horse discoloured dashinge myre waye dust wherby might appere late iourneyed also caused ride farre aboute theyr campes se whether trenche enuironed campe enlarged whyt furthermore marke whether trumpet sounde one two tymes within campe romaynes nothinge deceiued moche worde broughte campes nothynge enlarged twaine one liuius cosull l portius neither altered otherwise fyrste neuerthelesse troubled hym sore beinge wyse man moche vsed warres romaynes shewed hym trumpet blewe one pretor campe blewe two tymes wherfore iudged surely bothe consul whervppon began muse howe consull shulde departed brother anniball could deuyse thing brother illuded departinge capitayne campe whiche farre part power iudged susteined gret losse wherby durst followe consull wherfore feared greatly least whan lost come late brother socours also mistrusted letter neuer came anniballes handes messangers taken vp waye vpon syghte wherof consull come hast vanquishe also beinge great perplexitie caused fire put oute euery man trusse vp stuffe baggage begynninge nyghte hole host departed secretely folowinge two guide whoo farre gone partly feare partely beinge troubled rumour armye toke good hede waye wherfore secretely slypped awaye leauyng theim without guide wandered abrode fieldes beinge wery ouerwatched laide bowne slepe rest leauynge theyr standardes daye appered asdruball caused standardes go hoste alonge syde ryuer metaurus sekynge fordes myght passe ouer went vp riuer hyer bankes thus wanderynge styll crokes tourninges banke sekyng place passage spente great parte daye waste wherby romaynes gotten tyme space followe fyrst nero horseman ouer toke sone came lucius portius light harnessed men slewe many asdruball folke abode behynd fieldes rest asdruball seinge remedy escape soughte hyll riuer syde wheron myghte lodge host tyme liuius also come al power fotemen armed good array ioynynge theyr company gether put euery man order claudius nero led ryght wynge liuius kept lefte wyng portius pretor came myddell warde pwhan asdruball sawe remedy must needes fyght left fortifiyng campe put people array forefront set elephantes theim lefte hande agaynst claudius nero consull set frenchemen trusted theim moche hym selfe bicause thought ennemies feared theim ryghte wynge kepte hym selfe spanyardes olde meane warre moste truste liguriens men countrey italy sette middell behynde elephantes greatte hylse betwene frenchemen claudius nero meanes host might come fight theim wherfore stode styll good space without thing betweene asdruball liuius fyers mortall fyght greate numbre romayne fotemen agaynst multitude spaniardes expert warryours also agaynst liguriens wer stronge valiant men elephantes also dyd fyrste moche displeasure claudius seinge coulde haue doo frenchemen tourned aboute company fetchyng compasse came syde asdruballes armye spanyardes liguriens slayne party fyght alredy come frenchman able make smal resistence many company shronken away feble labour ouerwatchynge people well away peyne many theim slayne many also elephantes slayne romaynes moo theyr owne rulars rode vppon theim one stryken aferde beastes vnruly dyd soo moche hurte theyr owne carthaginenses hoste theyr owne kepers ryders slewe theim pasdruball lyke full noble capitayne handled hym selfe battayle sometyme fyght ng valiantly owne persone sometyme exhortyng men manfully fight sometyme desyred werye souldiours take peyne hym theyr owne lyues sometyme rebuked theyr sluggyshnes yf began flee anon brought backe battayle restored agayne fielde whyche diuers place slaked last whan saw helpe withoute remedy muste lose fielde myndynge lyue great slaughter men friendes whyche sake vndertooke voyage ranne horse spurres myddell romayne hoste declare noble valour stomacke whome descended lyke sonne amilcar brother anniball valyantly fought fyghtyng slayne greate slaughter sayde affricanes prysoners commaundynge theim goo anniball declare vnto hym ordre thynges hadde ben done battayl wherwith stryken sorowe bothe losse soo greate noumbee menne brother armye also losse friendes famylyars sayde knewe full well shoulde fortune fatall chaunce carthage within shorte space whervppon remoued fieldes brutians hadde power lefte hym men defende fortress yet helde farre gathered gyther metapontanes lucanes suche frendes brought countrey brutians remayned season counsailing beste hym doo p scipio dyuies battayles discom iteth carthaginenses taketh hanno yue dryucth hasdruball mage theyr power cleane spayne cap liiii spayne betwene romayns carthaginenses thus countrey diuyded asdruball sonne gysgon dryuen companye vttermoste parte spayne yles called gades rest countrey eastwardes vnder dominion romaynes onelesse fewe city whyche kepte affricanes whose succour hanno newe capitayne sent affrica newe armye steede asdruball slayne hanno also hyred great nomber men warre celtiberia great hoste ioyned mago agaynste whome scipio sent sillanus x footemen v c horseman passynge hye hilles manifold daungerous passage straites spayn made spede guyding certayne runawayes celtiberia came within ten myles ennemies knowledge hadde fame bruted comynge stode season tyll sayde runawayes espyes knowledge ennemies lodged ii campes celtiberiens left hande hye waie came frome campe healpe celtiberiens laste mago seinge parte lyke putte worste two thousande footemen wholle power horsemenne lefte lyue fledde vnto gades came asdruball hanno capytayne taken lyue many noble prysoners p soone battayle hanno cornelius scipio departed tarracon leauynge countrey l scipio brother tenne thousande fotemen one thousand horseman brother departing power assanted town qungin without peyne scarsely suffered put theyr scalinge ladder walles great violence dartes ingins whiche throwen sone raised vp thervnto men theron striuinge ascende anone eyther throwen downe men souldiours towne hauinge forkes made purpose orels ieoperdy drawen vp ladder men reason iron hokes throwen vpon ladder taking suche sure holde clymbers often time pulled vp farre frome grounde hanged longe roundes ladder thus continued assault long verye fyers daungerous bothe partes scipio deuided host thre partes intente one parte shulde euer assaulte towne rested wherfore commaunded whiche fyrst assaulte withdrawe tentes rest incontinent two partes freshe souldiours gaue newe assaulte two partes towne defondours beinge wery longe susteinyng furst assault also soore afraide desperate leauinge walles withdrewe wherupon towne wonne great occision made people kyndes age p whan tidinges noble acte brought p scipio capitiane gretly praysed brother hym moche honour myght sente hym rome assembled men lykewise able rencountre ennemies sente sillanus colchas kynge ruler ouer xxviii city townes iii footemen v c horseman h dde army came betula xlv horseman fotemen certaine day theyr metynge shyrmisshes iustes betwene horseman lighte fotemen bothe army last bothe descended fieldes al theyr power good order battayle middell wardes kept romaynes one syde carthaginenses affricanes syde wynges party spaniardes hyred souldiours thus stode redye battayle tyll night without stroke strikinge euen dyd certayne dayes folowynge euer bruted bothe army myddle wardes shulde still romaynes carthaginenses greatest strength noble experte men warre betwene also rested cause chiefe grounde warre scipio beinge aduertised ennemies trusted beleued order shulde kept still battayle againste daye wherin thought fight chaunged order fyrst euenyng commaunded horseman dawnynge day eate meate armed euery one haue horse also made redy battayle whiche commaundement diligently accomplished scipio sone day appered caused al horseman lyght armour inuade station campe carthaginenses rest hole hoste folowed good arraye otherwyse ordered eyther ennemies owne company loked put romaynes wynges middle put straungers hyred souldiours asdruball heringe greate noyse romayne horseman sodayne rumour feare owne menne ranne tente perceyued fieldes garnyshed ennemies sent forthe anone horseman romayn horseman sone hym selfe fotemen came forth campe kepyng rdre doue certayne dayes without chaungynge parte therof battayle betwene horseman endured longe whan host fotemen within half myle together scipio caused horseman withdrawe selues deuided two partes caused stande behynde two wynges euer redy theyr ayde succour nowe myddle warde spaniardes commaunded marche forwardes fast softe pace sente messanger sillanus martius gouerned lefte wynge chargyng make speede forwardes theyr partes lyke maner sawe hym ryght winge whiche ledde hym selfe wynges might fyghtyng good space myddle wardes shulde mete ordre wente forwardes spreadynge theyr wynges makynge great bosome myddell theyr hoste spanyardes middel went moch softer pace wynges wherby winges al redy come stroke fought long space affricans carthaginenses rested great strength theyr ennemies come stroke strikinge agayne bende part winges helpe theyr felowes foughte durste leste shulde open theyr battayle theyr ennemies whiche came directly vpon meanes winges wer anone ouercome dryuen myddell warde meruayle yong hyred souldiours spayne marched stronge olde warriours romaine latines agayne asdrubals men sodainely taken mornynge tyme receyue sustenaunce battayle wherfore whan daye somewhat spent waxed feynte feble intent scipio purposely tracted prolonged tyme myddell wardes shoulde mete ende heate sonne towardes myddell daye longe standynge harneis lacke meate drynke shulde take bothe theyr strength corage thus beinge wery assayled bothe middell warde also sydes romayne wynges constrained recule whiche dyd great whyle kepynge styll good ordre theyr withdrawynge asdruball continually cried therto exhorted sayinge wolde lyttell lyttell withdrawe shulde sone get mountaines whiche theyr backes shulde sure daunger theyr ennemies last seinge selues ouercome many theyr companye slayne partes theyr feare ouercame shame wherfore greate slaughter fledde theyr campe romaynes pursued faste taken theyr campe tentes vehement storme rayne sodeynly come vppon suche violence euery man gladde gette hym owne tent pauilion p carthaginenses althoughe nighte drewe faste sore wouded wet rayne wherby necessary occasion slepe rest yet afraide ceassed stylle strengthen fortifie campe dyches stone whiche gathered partes trustinge strength thereof theyr armour many hyred souldiours hoste carthaginenses lefte asdruball came scipio dyuerse stronge townes also delyuered vp hym garrison whiche left wherfore asdruball thinkynge hym selfe sure fleinge abydinge secretly departed thense nyghte p scipio mornynge aduertised departing ennemies sent horsemenne hym selfe army sodeynly folowed horseman length ouertoke made many skyrmyshes therby stayed tyll theyr hole armie fotemen also ouer toke great occuion made small resistence asdruball vii men hym fayne flee next hye mountayne encamped selues safe fro daunger hurt coulde done sone slypped then stale sea whiche farre toke shyppynge hym selfe mago fewe hym went iles beyonde furthest parte spayne called gades leauynge moste parte men behynde hym theyr owne aduenture prouide theim selues parte went romaynes parte city wer remayninge dominion carthaginenses p scipio downe walles earth place whiche hadde ben chiefe receptacle theyr ennemies myghte clerely defaced memorye therof abolysshed euer frome thense wente towarde castulo armie capytayne therof fearynge crueltie romaynes yelded towne carthaginenses also therin ascapa also strong towne martius brought subiection townes city fortress carthaginenses helde thus clerelye expelled oute spayne xiiii yere
