tyme come citie rome althoughe came frome diuers partes wherefore agreed euer theim came fyrste citie preneste shulde tary comynge felowe accordyng appoyntement mette bothe one baye frome thense sent messangers citie desyrynge senatours mete house bellona goddes warre third day folowing wer receiued great multitude senator citezins goodly salutation great thankes theyr politike gouernance roumes whose helpe dexteritie comon welth nobly preserued aduaunced soone brought senate accordinge olde custome conquerours declared theyr noble actes whiche achieued common welthe citie rome desyred fyrst honour myghte giuen immortall goddes mighte triumphe entre citie whiche theyr request graunted touchinge maner theyr entringe triumphe appoynted shuld come seuerally together vainquished theyr ennemies together agreed also betwene selues bicause victorye prouince liuius also bicause liuius army come rome nero host coulde wyse brought thither therfore shuld liuius ride charyot souldiours order followe hym nero shuld ryde hym horsebacke without souldiours folowe hym claudius contented gyue honour felowe whiche gentilnes wan moche honour praise euery man said horsebacke vi dais ridden length italy fought asdruball border fraunce time anniball iudged hym apulia onely name able kepe anniball lurkyng campe onely comyng cause victory asdrubal wherfore said ride one consull neuer highe charyot yet consul rode horsebacke worthy triumph ye although nero dyd go fote yet worthye glory fame perpetual prayses folowed nero capitoly palaice rome presented moche money theyr gayne put treasory morowe consul also horseman praysed moche l veturius q cecilius desiring might next yere folowing chosen consul next election done bothe appoynted ii consul army kepe warre agaynst anniball p thynges putte good order departed citie wente countrey lucanes shorte tyme brought countrey subiection anniball lyttell doone offered hym selfe gyue battayle discouraged losse brother frendes souldiours parte consulles thought best prouoke hym battayle se founde hym noo sturrynge moche feared estemed valour noble capytayne whome prayse gyuen noo man coulde iudge hym whether commended tyme prosperitie tyme aduersitie woulde wonder se maynteyned warre farre frome countrey full space thyrtene yeres lande ennemies hauynge armye owne citie countreye gathered togyther many nation whyche lyued vnder one maner lawe neyther hadde one custome language moche different apparayle armour customes ceremony ye hadde seuerall goddis yet dydde gouerne theim knytte theim gyther suche amitie man coulde iudge knowe dyssention betweene theym insurrection agaynste theyr capytaynes althoughe dyuerse tymes lacked paye theyr wage also vitayles sustenaunce lacke whereof warres moche inconuenience hathe ensewed agayne deathe asdruball armye whome trust whan italy taken frome hym saue onely countrey corner brutians woulde wonder see noo rebellyon amongest owne menne consyderynge vyttayles hadde lyttell angle brutians whyche yf hadde beene wholly tylled sowed hadde beene able susteyne soo greate armye neuer lesse greatte parte therof vntylled parte feare romaynes theyr friendes partely mooste parte yonge menne countreye taken warres whyche wonte tylle man grounde husbandrye thinges say conferred togither wyll make al men muse howe coulde quietly gouerne greate hoost prayse greatly wyse conduict therin p scipio asdruball arriue one daie affrica lodged bothe togyther palays kynge syphax cap lvi departynge p scipio tarracon carthaginenses beinge dryuen spayne massanissa seinge great falle frendes carthaginenses secretely communication sillanus wone sure frende romayns whervppon haue frendes affrica obedyent redy hym necessity appoynted sayle ouer countrey make hym selfe stronge myght ayde succour romaynes whan neede requyred sillanus soone retourned scipio tarracon p p scipio wylling certifie senate great victory happie chaunces sente brother l scipio rome rehersed ledde hym many noble men prisoner whome hadde taken warres whervppon meruaylousely honoured praysed men yet alone hadde deserued sayde honour estemed feates done spayne nothyng comparison thynges whyche conceyued mynde looked conqueste greate carthage affrica ende warre consummation honour glory wherfore worke tyme thinges afterwardes shoulde serue pourpose determyned wynne vnto hym harte princis whyche borderars vnto countrey fyrste mynded attempt kynge syphax p syphax kyng people affrica called masesuli adioynyng moore lying side sea mediterrane ouer new carthage spain tyme great friende carthaginenses hym sent c lelius goodly present wherwith kynge verye gladde well pleased consyderynge mynde good fortune whyche romaynes hadde partes seynge power olde friendes carthaginenses soo greately decayed italy hadde nowe lyttell doo spayne nothynge agreed lelius become friende romaynes sayde woulde procede confirmation amitie betweene tyll myghte personally speake scipio chief capitayn romaynes whervppon lelius takynge assuraunce hym safe goynge commynge capitayne retourned scipio declared vnto hym howe spedde declared scipio indgynge frendshyppe great helpe furtheraunce purpose touchynge desyrous affayres affrica bothe greatte strengthe rychesse also countrey adioynyng carthage directly ouer agaynste spayne leauynge lucius martius tarracon sillanus newe carthage power sufficient defence spayne lelius two galeys rowbarges fyue oores piece passed ouer affrica p nowe happened euen tyme asdruball late ben dryuen spayne newely arryued hauen seuen galeys castyng ankers drewe neere shore coulde asdruball perceyuinge two galeys rowbarges scipio comynge towardes hauen knewe full welle vesselles ennemyes wherefore doubtynge beynge soo fewe numbre myght easyly oppressed vanquys hed shoulde gette hauen commaunded folkes wey vp ankers make theim redy sette furthe speede hauynge good wynde theyr furtherance entred hauen galeys asdruball myght gette suche ruffelinge noise littell shifte made men wherefore romaynes one gotten kinges hauen man durste bolde meddell theym thus wente two capyteynes lande fyrste asdruball scipio lelius bothe wente kynges palayes whose comynge dydde vnto syphax greatte honour neuer seene gouernoures ii noble seignories dayes world came euer palayce vpon one day desire amitie peace kynge ryght gentylly receyued theim bothe sen theyr chaunces mete one time howse dydde myght brynge communication trustynge therby appease stryfe discorde mattier hadde beene betweene theym scipio refused doo affyrmynge pryuate matter displeasure betweene hym asdruball whyche communication hearynge friendes neded determined neyther thynge touchynge common welthe countrey wherin might trauayle intreate onelesse speciall auctoritie commaundement wholle senate kynge made great instance scipio seinge bothe guestes one wolde contented ordered myghte haue cause expelle theim bothe frome table scipio kynges requeste onely contented sytte asdruball oone table also kynges pleasure laye bedde dyd scipio naturally suche dexteritie conformable reason thereby onely wanne herte syphax alsoo broughte mooste mortall ennemye asdruball admyration hym hadde seene conuersation euer dydde acte euer dydde wherevppon beganne coniecture iudge syphax myghte become friende romaynes suche polycie deemed scipio haue wynnynge hertes men beganne dyuise necessary carthaginenses consult among theim selues spayne loste myghte recouered rather howe myghte keepe domynion affrica specyally moued thus doubte iudged soo greatte capytayne romaynes woulde leaue countrey lately hadde conquered wander abrode straunge domynyon onely two galeys leauynge behynde hym greatte power committyng hym vnto daungier vnknowen kynge onely vppon truste therby wynne affrica p scipio concludinge peace amitie kynge departed hym leauynge asdruball wrapped manyfolde trouble within foure dayes susteynynge many stormes sea arriued safegard newe carthage p massanissa speaketh secretely scipio entreth leage romaynes mago sayleth italy ioyne anniball cap lvii declared howe sillanus secrete communication massanissa wonne hym friende romaynes conclusyon communication deferred tyll massanissa myghte speake scipio personallye sure faythfull assurance theyr alliaunce whiche caused p scipio enterpryse longe peynfull iourney come nere sea side mete hym whose approchynge massanissa yle called gades aduertised l martius fained mago horse lost spylt longe kepte within yle without exercise men also empayred throughe idlenes puttynge selues vre feates armes furthermore saide longe lienge ilande caused derth scarsitie thynges wherfore desired licence mighte horseman passe ouer spayne spoyle wast countrey nere sea syde p perswasyon obteyned lycence came ouer spayne fyrste arryuaile sente thre noble men numidie scipio wherof wylled reteyne hym two pledge sende againe third theim acertayne hym tyme place theyr metynge whose conducte myght broughte place appoynted daye came met gether smalle numbre companye massanissa fyrste syghte althoughe greate admyration scipio throughe noble fame actes yet vppon syght hym presence hym moche veneration besydes nature indowed goodlye large stature wherein shewed marueylouse magnifycence yet set forthe reason goodly long heare comly apparell manly warrelyke fashion also myddle age full strength become beautyfull sickenes whiche late recouered lusty youthe semed renewed wherby pleasaunt beholde theyr first metyng massanissa half astonied gaue hym humble thankes goodnesse shewed sendynge home brother sonne prisoner tyme sayde ceassed seke occasion friendshyp amitie whiche nowe obteyned gaue thankes goddes trustynge wold apply himselfe affayres romaynes cause theyr common welthe neuer aduaunced one man beinge straunger vnto harty beneuolence good wyll bare coulde neuer althoughe wolde haue shewed hym spayne beinge hym straunge vnknowen countrey case romaynes wolde sende scipio theyr capitayne affrica bred brought vp doubted hie seruice honour carthage shuld longe endure p scipio gladly behelde hym also heard hym knowinge surely chiefe al horseman army ennemies lusty yonge man nobleherte courage wherfore entreated theyr busines giuynge faythe one faythfull loue amity departed scipio tarracon massanissa ile gades bycause myghte appere mago done feate spayne scipio suffered spoile certayne goodes groundes sea cost take praye hym p mago beinge desperate good spede hadde spayne mynde sayle affrica sodeynlye letter came hym carthage commaundyng hym nauy shyppes gades shulde sayle ouer italy hyringe moche people myghte frenchemen liguriens shoulde spede ioyn selfe annibal purpose great summes money sent carthage besydes leuied exacted moch money coulde gaditanes compellinge euery man brynge money besydes spoyled temple rich arryued ile minorque gathered together ii yonge men beginnynge sommer toke hym fayled ouer italy xxx great shippes warre many shyppes loden prouisyon hoste tyme xii fotemen two horseman numbre sodeynlye arriued geene whiche towne toke small resystence beinge vnprouyded men warre thense sayled alonge costes liguria nexte mountaynes called alpes letter rome senate aduertisynge asdruball ii yeres paste slayne armye frontier italy great comfort citie great ioye vaine passed lyke shadowe onlesse prouyded nowe spedye remedy newe armye come mago carthage begynne newe warre lyke onelye capytayne therof chaunged newes moued moch senatours wherfore sente letter liuius proconsull commaundynge hym brynge host hetruria arminius cn seruilius pretour banner displayed ennemies howe many cyties taken strength people brought theyr obeysaunce shewed also hadde fought iiii sundry capitaines noble men vanquished army whiche neuer vanquished nowe carthaginenses lefte spayne al noble actes admitted entre citie triumph bicause neuer borne office citie counsayle arose entred citie presented brought tresory great plenty money rich gaynes prayes iourney affrica willyng mayntein warres anniball italy cap lix purpose scipio senatours consulted togyther amonge desyred q fabius maximus declare opinyon aunswered making oration maner fourme folowynge p well assured father conscript yf dissent agree hasty passage affrica two thynges wyll iudged spoken one slownes slacke tractynge mattier whiche naturally gyuen yongemen calle fearefulnes slouthe greueth lyttell thoughe haue suche opinion sen men councelles heretofore haue appered gloryous fyrste face lengthe counsaile hath euer proued beste moste common welthe seconde thynge shoulde euyll wyl go aboute hynder glory valyaunt consull daily groweth encreaseth frome whyche suspition yf neyther fascion lyuynge maners offyce dictatour whiche haue borne roume consull whiche haue fyue time enioyed neyther greate glorye haue wonne tyme peace warre wyl delyuer pourge lette myne age least deliuer therefro indifferent contention betwene hym yeres may matche sonne dictatour mayster horse laboured senate made equall auctoritye rule whyche thynge neuer seene yet neuer manne herde eyther priuyly openly refuse theyr ordre therin hadde leauer gette deedes woordes whyche mennes iudgement compared shoulde shortely owne confessyon gyue preferrement moche lesse nowe whan haue oft borne honourable office dooe intende stryue flourysshynge younge manne letted anniball vyctory intent myghte nowe vanquysshed lusty stronge reason woulde pub cornelius ye shoulde contented sen dy dde neuer sette myne owne fame honour fame people dyd common welth although preferre honour laudis common welth neuer lesse case warre italy elles suche ennemy whose vanquyshing small honour gotten would kepe italy although commune welthe therby somewhat anaunced myght seeme go aboute take thy glory sen anniball ennemy hath hooste xiiii yeeres vexed italy shouldest thou p cornelius thynke lose honour thy prowesse beynge consull thou canste expelle driue hym cuntrey hath cause many men slaughter great distruction wherby luctatius bare away honourable title fynyshyng firste warre carthaginenses euen soo nowe thou mayste obteyne prayse fynyshing warre onelesse thou doest thynke amilcar capitayn preferred anniball warre victory noble gloryous shall thy chaunce consull ouercome thinkest thou honour deliuer spayne frome ennemies delyuer italy anniball suche man euer wyll chose warre place muste reckened rather feare hym dispyse hym make redy therfore thynke fetche compasse aboute busshe goo affrica intente anniball shoulde folowe goo nexte waye woorke euer anniball thyther dyrecte thy warre nature gyueth manne fyrst defend owne countrey inuade assaile lande lette firste peace italy warre affrica lette feare fyrste expelled v driuen vpon yf thou canste thy gouernaunce bothe fyrste ouercome anniball assayle carthage treasorye able finde ii greate armyes one affrica sufficient fynde p licinius one host italy p scipio also affrica yf shuld chance god forbyd yet suche happes haue happed maie dooe agayne anniball dyd ouercome licinius comynge towardes rome myght call frome affrica dydde call quintus fuluius frome capua succour ye affrica also fortune warre doubtfull nowe contention debate betwene bicause fraied forein power sone romain army shal appere theim wil straight ioyne selfes together towne fier house people wyll assemble together quenchyng thereof feare strength townes perceyuing italy made bare men warre thy coming thither power wil sende newe army affrica italy wyll commande mago already come costes liguriens ioyne anniball power shall case wherein asdruball passed mounteynes descended italy stronger valyant capytaine thou arte moore oughte italy reioyce keepe styll amonge v thou canst deny thy self anniball head strength warre thou sayst thy goinge affrica shall drawe anniball thyther soo whether ann bal thou must chefly haue praye aunswere shalt thou sure affrica beinge alone italye hauinge consull thy felowe host ioyned thou wilte seke experience therof let claudius liuius late consulles exaumple lernynge agayne whether shall anniball stronger lyttle angle brutiens wherunto dryuen hole hoste shall come carthago hauynge al friendes dissemble truly q fabius wyll equall vnto renowme also passe prayses yf may atteyne thervnto lette neyther v bothe thynke none shall come v shall lyke vnto v desyre greate hurt hynderaunce bothe posteritie also common welth generally mankynde furthermore fabius hath remembred ieoperdies peryls shulde entre goynge affrica though carefull bothe myne army meruaile greatly whens louing care thought sodeinly spronge whan father myn vncle wer bothe slayne bothe theyr army almoste distroied slayne cleane loste affricanes ouerrounnynge countrey iiii seuerall hoostes capytaines woulde man offre hym selfe capitayne romaine spayne onely atwhychetyme whan people citie made gouernor tha xxiiii yeres old man founde whiche would remembre tendre age neyther power ennemies daungerousnes people rome secondely throughe truste goddes whiche witness truse broken theim thyrdely occasyon offered syphax massanissa whose promyse faythe wyll soo truste wyll also well ware theyr falsehode said gate ny came forth battayl without good order massanissa faining selfe afraide somewhat reculed sometime turned fought folowed thus played base tyll whole multitude horsemenne come furthe yates forthe tyme thus syphax toke aduyse asdruball asdruball noble menne carthage espyes leysar viewe serche thynges charged scipio hadde tyme prepare mete serue purpose numidiens also carthaginenses peace romaynes onlesse wolde leaue amitie carthaginenses tyme truse expyred sprynge yere come wherefore scipio brynge pourpose aboute assembled gether shippes furnished theim ordynaunce artyllery whiche knewe wayes entree kinges campe soo laide numidiens embushmetes people ran abrode quenche fyre fel company theyr ennemies er knew meanes many slaine many also wer burned theyr beddes fyre see citie carthage also sea bette walles towne p whyles romaynes castynge trenche fortifiynge towne tunnes perceyued nauy carthaginenses saylynge towardes vtica scipio leauyng woorkes made haste men sophonisba wyfe kinge spphax cap lxiiii morowe battaile fought kyng syphax escaped declared scipio sent lelius massanissa romayn horsmen lyghtest harneissed footemen also numidian folowe kyng asdruball while went wynne townes countrey adiacent carthage within xv dayes came numidia whose coming people therof called masesuli receiued gladly massanissa deliuered hym whole realme theyr ryghtfull kynge whose cominge longe desyred expellynge cleane city fortress therof garnysons syphax soo glad kepe hym within bondes owne realme harte swelled displeasure wyllynge reuenged whervnto wyfe father moche intyced hym prycked hym forwardes hadde great plentie men also horse whyche moche encouraged hym make newe fielde wherefore assembled many thoughtable gyuyng theim horse harneys diuydynge horseman footemenne companyes appoyntynge theim capitaines accordynge learned romaynes thus hauyng thinges redynesse marched towardes ennemies great hooste almoste newe souldiours yonge men like end part consyder well bothe infirmitie man power fortune know actes subiect chance knowlage case thou woldist haue come desire peace toke grettrauaile come affrica thou haddest thy good wil departed thine army italy denied thy requeste might well haue iudged haue wrought proudely stubburnely euen haue drawe thy power home affrica thou arte redy make v resistence seinge peace truce one taken whiche ye haue broken taking shippes force tyme truce violatinge embassadours may ryghte well honour byd prepare warre sen could hold contented peace whan ye thus without agrement peace ii capytaines brake communication departed euery one company determining try matter battail take suche fortune goddis wolde gyue theim p soone come campes openly bothe partes gaue commaundement souldiours make redy fyght theyr last battaile wherby ca dyd ouercome shulde haue felicitie one day euer next nyght shuld know whether rome carthage shuld haue superioritie onely italye affrica worlde whiche shulde rewarde nowe hym shuld haue victory contrary part peryll ieoperdye lesse declared part whiche shulde haue worse battayle romaynes hadde place whether flye beinge straunge countrey carthage muste nedes come vtter distruction case last army refuge vanquished ouerthrowen p great ieopardy next day ii valyant capitaynes two noble rychest people sette furthe ii myghty army intendynge day eyther increase honour whiche gotten el ouerthrowen lose hoope feare myngled bothe togyther theyr myndes whan sawe theyr owne battaile battayle ennemies conceiued myndes ioye sorowe souldiours fayled remembre theyr capitaines declared vnto theim greate warnynges exhortation anniball rehersed people theyr actes done italy many romayne capytaynes howe many armyes hadde slayne scipio shewed conquestes spayne also late affrica confessyon ennemyes feare constrayned requyre peace although theyr vntrouth wold suffre theim kepe whan wherfore gessed goddis appointed theim fyght bataile lyke successe lucke wha fought yle egates sayd warre trauayle end spoyle carthage euen hande whyche ye shall retourne home countreye youre parentes wyues chylderne owne goodes comfortable woordes sette furthe suche gesture bodye merye countenaunce though hadde al redy hadde vyctory ennemies afterward putte men order first spearemen chiefe mooste assured footemen greate multitude togyther standarde smalle bandes whyche shoulde certayne space distaunt one intent elephantes theyr ennemyes myghte come betweene sayde bandes receyued theim without breakynge arraye voyde space betweene sayde bandes appoynted dyuers lyghtest harneysed souldiours stande fulfyll voyde place commaundynge theim whan elephantes pressed theim shuld recule behynde sayd bandes whyche array el steppe among went standerdes forefront battaile sette elephantes whyche numbre lxxx whome put ordre suche nation hyred came succour liguriens frenchemen men iles named baleares called maiorque minorque myngled amonge great numbre moore seconde battaile sette carthaginenses affricanes legion lacedemonians sent thither succour carthaginenses philip kyng macedome within lyttell space theim placed italian cam whan left cuntrey winges wer horseman left winge helde numidian horseman right wynge carthaginenses hoste annibal wer men diuers nation cuntreis diuers tunges langages also different lawes armour aparaile euery one gaue sundry diuers exhortation either feare comfort suche come succour promysed great rewarde pray whiche shulde wonne industry trauaile liguriens promised plentiful reward fertile pleasaunt fieldes italy moore numidian exhorted well feare leste shulde el greuous seruitude massanissa frenchemenne wer set naturall hatred bare romaynes carthaginenses put remembrance fight walles naturall cuntrey propre goodes sepulchre elder child parentes trembling wiues meane way sayde put betwene hope feare either must suffre miserable seruitude distruction citie cuntrey orels obteine empire worlde p tyme noble capitayn finyshed wordes romaynes blewe vp theyr trumpettes horne makynge terrible noyse clamour greate numbre elephantes beinge furyouse tourned backe vppon theyr companye specially vppon lefte wynge moore numidian whiche perceyued well massanissa wherefore also inuaded wing horseman putting theim suche feare fledde leauynge syde hoste bare succour dyuers elephantes force wer constrained entre myddle battaile whome anone lyght armed souldiours gaue place suffryng theim entre among theim thrust speares innelyns many slain lelius horsmen assailed right wing horsme carthage puttig also slight body host side left without defence horsme winges chased away tha began battel fotemen strog partes great wer cry wer made roman wer better corage stronger hope stregth wherfore short space caused enmies giue back certain space groud wha thei ons gote grounde theyr shyeldes targettes came still thrusting theyr ennemies bearing backe tyl sone fyrste battayle tourninge theyr backes began flie came second battayle carthaginenses moore wolde suffer entre leste shulde cause theyr arraye broken wherfore betwene theyr owne fellowes began great debate slaughter soo carthaginenses constrayned fyghte bothe theyr owne vnruly felowes also romaynes theyr ennemies neuerthelesse wolde wyse receyue theyr felowes fledde amonge leste shulde mengle fearefull sorte whiche flyghte hurte wounded amonge earnestly bent fight whiche myght haue turned moche theyr dyspleasure dryuing away heapes compelled go gether one side theym abrode fieldes great occision made moche romaynes coulde come fyghte carthaginenses fyrste muste peyne go ouer dead body slayne scipio caused troumpet blowen withdrawe men first battayle ben sore traueyled many sore wounded caused stand behinde rereward made rerewarde best men auaunce forewarde vpon carthaginenses beganne battayle newe agayne whiche sore fierse came romaynes assured strongest men expert warres beinge vanquished twyse nowe lothe ashamed vanquished romaynes farre moin noumbre taken great courage dryuinge awaye bothe wynges also forewarde theyr ennemies p whyles thus foughte seconde battayle lelius massanissa returned theyr horseman chase wynges carthaginenses power violence came backes seconde battayle carthaginenses whiche busy valiauntly fought able endure theyr violence force put flyght slayne partes day slayne taken carthaginenses aboute xl men many elephantes many standardes noble men taken battayll great also praye spoyle founde campe romanes toke brought shippes romaynes also lost battayle aboue x men anniball fewe fledde adrument neuer departed field til bothe battayle assayed asmoche possyble done safegard people wherin day prayse bothe scipio al expert men warre romains specially ordering battayl fyrst set forefront great nomber elephantes whose gret strength intollerable violence shuld breke arraye romaine putting order whyche halfe wynnynge battail set foremost hyred souldiours diuers nation intent confused nombre stranger fought great faith loue onely money sholde haue place tyme flee battayle also intent suche stranger shuld endure fyrst violence ennemies makyng wery weake chiefe men trust haue thyng theim carthaginenses affricans trustie souldiours last al good space behinde theim placed italiens people whome knew wel whether shuld friendes foe thus pollicie wolde serue hym yet fynishinge warre whiche achieued scipio traueile great daungier cause scipio counsaylours wer fully minded take peace carthaginenses wherefore nexte day called legate carthage greatly rebukinge vntrewth diuers time shewed wyllynge theim nowe last beinge taughte good experience regarde bothe theyr goddes theyr othes shewinge hauing pitie destruction theim theyr soo noble citie contented graunte peace vpon condition fyrste shoulde lyue free theyr owne lawes customes enioyinge suche city townes affrica hadde possession warre betwene theim taken frome daye forthe romaynes shulde destroye spoyle parte therof agayne carthaginenses shulde restore romaynes suche person fled runne away romayns prisoner romains theyr friendes captiuite also shoulde delyuer theim theyr shyppes warre shyppes excepte onely galeys hauynge thre order oores piece shoulde also delyuer vp theyr elephantes whiche alredye tamed made apte warre neyther shulde tame moo agayne shoulde moue warre affrica withoute affrica lycence commaundemente romaynes furthermore shulde restore vnto massanissa suche thynges hadde taken makynge peace agrement hym also yelde vnto romayne hoste wheate wage vnto return legate rome besydes shulde paye x talentes syluer fyftye yeres durynge whiche tyme shulde yerely paye summe deuyded euen portion paymente wherof perfourmaunce condytions shoulde delyuer hym c pledge owne election wherof none shuld vnder thage xiiii yeres neither aboue thage xxx vpon condition agreed giue truce wolde delyuer hand suche hulkes shyppes burthen fraught implementes carthaginenses toke theim duringe laste tyme truse graunted theim elles shulde neither loke truse peace p whan legate come carthage co maunded declare condition peace openly congregation people therevnto assembled condition one gysgo noble man carthage spake sore wold haue dissuaded people taking peace whose sayinges many vnruly multitude gaue good audience annibal therwith greatly moued went force drewe downe rudenesse maner whan departed citie ix yeres olde whiche nowe xxxvi yeres agone time haue sufficiently knowen instructed feates warre beinge taught chaunces fortune euen frome chyldehoode wherfore syncerely intreate peace amonge noble carthage one asdruball called hedus one chiefe theim bothe auctoritie nobilitie euer desyrous peace held moche agaynste anniball affinitie asdruball sayde fewe couetous personnes citie culpable warre comminaltie faultes whyche layde theym excused confessed leste denying myght worse hearde senate perswaded senatours vse theyr prosperous fortune gentylly due temperance professynge euer case carthaginenses would haue folowed myndes hym hanno takynge tyme whan offered beene gyuers peace vppon suche condition nowe gladde take others handes sayde seldome sene good fortune good mynd gyuen one men cause conquestes romains euer chiefly hath prosperitie ye haue remembrance consulte thynges come empyre hath bene encreased gentylnes fauour shewed nation ye haue vanquyshed hath bene victory gotten theim p asdruball finysshed oration ambassadours made moche lamentable proposition bewayling miserable fall state carthaginenses greattest lordes honour worlde nowe constrayned abyde enclosed within walles citie hauyng nothing el myghte clayme propretie ye citie helde vpon goodnes forbearyng romaynes while theyr pleasure forbere vtter distruction therof humble gentyll woordes senatours vniuersally fully inclyned peace one senatours spake loude voyce peace graunted carthaginenses goddis shall sweare make peace whan haue broken promise deceiued goddis sware herte madnesse frenesie neuer lesse laughter inordinate cometh time teares shuld haue wept armour taken fro shippes burned eies libertie makinge warres straunger onely lycence romaynes taken frome wherin rested chiefe vndoinge greattest falle ye fele hurte onelesse touche priuate welthe great hurte common welthe ye neyther fele regarde ennemies greate spoyle vyctorie carthage remayned alone naked without armour defence among many armed men affrica man wepte mourned nowe ye must pay tribute owne priuate goodes euery man wepeth ye wolde burienge friendes feare sore ye shall shortly perceyue ye wepte leaste harmes worst behinde p peace thus cocluded betwen romains carthaginenses scipio calling people together besides restored vnto massanissa father kyngedome also gaue citie cyrtha townes groundes wonne syphax afterwarde caused cn octauius delyuer cn cornelius newe consull nauy brought sicilia caused embassadours carthage go towardes rome haue thinges confirmed auctoritie senate whiche auctoritie romayne legate concluded p thus thynges beinge peace sea lande army toke shippynge sayled ouer sicilia thense italye met men countrey great honour ioye gladde euery man bothe peace victorye poore men townes city waye went towarde rome ran forthe se hym prayse hym thus greate honour came rome receiued citie mooste noble triumphe enryched citie greate mmes golde syluer claudius marcellus terentius culleo try whether information made true commanding publishe abrode cause theyr coming determine certaine matter controuersie wer betwene carthagineses king massanissa none p tale published beleued true common people anniball therwith could blinded knewe full well onely cause theyr comminge wherfore thynkinge season gyue place till time might better serue hym ii greatly losse honour also dominion wold haue caused hym leaue possession certayne city also shuld medle grece shulde moue warre determyned anniball greatly fauour chieifly thought expert man mete fotemenne one thousande horseman wyll power sayle affrica trusting cause carthaginenses rebel agaynste romaynes case wyll folowe request yet wyll inuade part italy moue warre romaynes maye sayde kyng ambassadours hauyng knowledge kyng antiochus lyttell gone agaynste pisidians fyndyng annibal diuers time resorted vnto familyar communication onely intent make haue good opinion romaynes mystruste thyng intended theym agaynste among communication betwen ambassadours annibal remembred scipio demaunded whome iudged noble capitayne euer knewe hearde whome anniball aunswered alexander macedony smal power ouercame many nation vanquished many greate army battayle traueylynge many straunge farre cuntreis whiche passed power witte mannes cumpasse scipio demaunded hym iudged seconde noble capytayn aunswered pyrrbus wyse expert man placinge campes fortifieng fortress watche ward getting hertes men vnto obeysaunce soo muche warred italye italyens gladder vnder gouernaunce beynge straungyer vnder dominion power romaynes demaunded scipio whome thoughte thyrde withoute fayle sayde selfe whych aunswere scipio laughed sayde wouldest thou haue sayd case thou haddest ouercome battayle haue done treuly sayde anniball woulde haue putte myselfe bothe alexander pyrrhus also aunswere seemed scipio straunge proude whereby mynded take scipio al glory p durynge longe taryenge romayne legate ephesus nothynge el wrought often metynge communication theym anniball made kynge suspecte mystrust whervpon called councel p agayn one thoas etholien desirous haue kyng power arryue grece withoute partynge strengthe sayde vnto hym syr greatte citie demetrias part city grece loke daylye commynge thyther agaynste arryuayle ye shall see countreye assemble seasyde sone may watch perceyue nauy comynge sea touchyng parting shyppes power wyse allowe case ye mynded anniball men vnmete haue rule gouernance therof p fyrst ye must consyder said thoas annibal carthaginens outlaw banished man fro cuntrey whose crafty witte wyl imagyne dayly newe deuyses euen fortune dothe varye shall fall brayne agayne yf shoulde chaunce annibal loose nauie men vanquyshed losse wil lesse capitayne loste theym case shoulde happen hym haue vyctorye honour therof shall wholly abyde anniball antiochus furthermore fortune well serue anniball vtterly subdue romaynes ye thynke continue subiection whiche cuntrey culd suffre self obedience nay said youth hath euer coueted minde emperour hole world age neuer contented vnder rule may chose wherfore cousayl ye haue nede make annibal capitain please ye may vse copany fred iourney takig aduise affayrs prudet counsailour none otherwise p crafty vntrew cousail thoas turned kiges mynde cleane frome sendynge anniball army affrica thoughte mete necessary wherfore prepared sayl grece help etholiens wanne certayn citi last consul atulius army romains came socors frendes great mounteyne whiche passethe throughe myddle grece fought antiochus put flyght sleyngal host except onely v c fled kyng p whiche discomfiture antiochus annibal smalle nomber men lefte hym battaylle cam see toke shipping came ephesus remayned thynkyng selfe sure oute daunger romayns perswaded beleue many gladde please mynd many suche dissembler haue beene shall dayly greatte prynces onely anniball aduysed kynge prepare commynge romaynes sayenge meruayled already arryued rather commynge myghte loked shewynge also romayns stronge valiant vpon see land doubtyng shortely wold striue dominion asia eyther muste take theim empire el shuld dangier lose kyngdome knewe desire ruler ouer worlde counselynge loke none thyng handes case shuld deceiue self vayne false hope p long beginnynge warres grece l cornelius scipio c lelius choosen consulles whiche election p scipio affricanus offered senate case would grant brother l scipio countrey grece prouynce would gladly take payne go iourney wherunto senate agreed geuynge also auctoritie go asia thought expedient sayenge woulde nowe proue whether antio hus holpen counsayl anniball vanquyshed romain consull army help scipio made great conquest affrica army shippes made ready consull arriued grece sone receyuing many rebell city handes thense sayled asia licence kynge philyp passage throughe macedony trace kyngdome antiochus p dyuers battaylles foughte vppon sea betweene romayne nauy polixenidas capitayne kynges shyppes euer romaynes victory help kyng eumenes also rhodiens laste chaunced soonne scipio affricanus taken prisoner brought antiochus kepte honorably gentelly afterward trustyng haue frendshyp p scipio healpe peace made betwene romaynes sente home sonne withoute payeng raunsome perceyued romaynes approche nere vnto thought better common peace battayle trustyng haue easy condition peace moued tyme matter came communication betwene consulle kynges embassadours condition peace sore antiochus refused take theim althoughe thervnto perswaded letter p scipio affricane wherevpon bothe partyes prepared theim fyghte battayle cruel last kyng antiochus put fiyght liiii footemen slayne horseman iiii besydes iiii c taken prysoners small losse romayns sent antiochus eftsones embassadours consull peace lengthe meanes p scipio affricanus graunted vpon condition p fyrste shoulde frome thense foorthe make warre europe alsoo shoulde leaue possessyons city landes countreyes whyche syde greatte mountayne called taurus agayne shoulde paye romaynes fyftene thousande talentes xii yeres pay vnto king eumenes iii hundred talentes great quantitie wheate vpon condytions shoulde haue peace prouyded anniball authour warre thoas dyuerse capytaynes counsaylloures myghte bee delyuered vnto hym kynge beynge extreeme myschyeffe receyued peace vppon sayde condytyons putte perfourmance ther pledge peace also confirmed senate rome p thynges thus prosperously brought passe l scipio consull returned rome receyued citie great honour triumphe brother victory affrica named affricanus conquestes asia called asiaticus honour succession euer p anniball fleith prusias kyng bithynia howe ended lyfe cap lxxiiii anniball battayle begon betwene romains antiochus wherin vanquished fledde mistrustinge folowed kynge necessitie must dryuen take peace whiche feared leste romaynes bearyng hym mortall malyce wold require delyuerie thoughte prouyde hym selfe tyme wherfore incontinent fledde prusias kyng bithynia longe taryed quintius flaminius sent rome kynge shewinge hym senatours thought delte friendly kepe realme theyr great capitall ennemy annibal man made fyrste owne countrey make warre vtter vndoinge thense came antiochus autour also warre romaynes nowe repayred vnto hym thought woulde tourne vndoinge prusias wyllynge gratyfy romaynes deuysed eyther slee hym el take delyuer hym flaminius wheruppon incontinente seruauntes kynge also flaminius besette house anniball rounde coulde waye issue anniball foreseinge hatred romaynes bare hym small fayth prynces specially lyghtnes prusias therfore thynkynge haue waye flie daungier nede required deuysed vii wayes entree house wherof certayne secrete priuie numbre great men armes whiche house watche straightly kept kynges commaundement euer offered issue espyed embushementes harney men tyme death drawe nere called poyson whiche longe tyme hym euer redy suche chaunces sayde nowe wyll delyuer romaynes great thought haue longe tyme taken bringe confusion althoughe nowe olde yet thynke longe dye deathe bothe flaminius theyr legate shal haue small victory blaming detestable falshede prusias cruelly wolde suffer murther friend receyued keping drunke empoysoned drinke sone dyed p lamentable ende ryght wyse noble valyaunte capytayne anniball straunge region exiled banyshed owne natiue countrey aboute time longe worthye romayne scipio affricanus also dyed romaynes manyfold benefites shewed recompenced detestable ingratitude certayne citie beinge ennemies man authoritie escape enuye charged hym olde matier betwene pleminius locrenses wherin sayde consul corrupted money therfore ministred iustice agayne layde agaynst hym delyuerye sonne beinge prisoner antiochus withoute raunsome whiche thoughte suspecious smalle cause called senate though ben meane persone put aunswere extremitie without fauour hauynge respecte noble actes done common weale whiche ingratitude toke displesantly departynge court went countreye towne lytarne dwelled long lyued exilynge hym selfe rome euer deathe commaunded body buried also bone myght rest vnkynde countrey p thus ii worthyest city worlde found vnkynde theyr noble ruler capytaynes one tyme carthage banyshed anniball vanquished rome exiled scipio vanquished ennemies wherin twayne blamed ingratitude finis londini aedibus thomae bertheleti regii impressoris typis excusum anno verbi incarnati x l cvm privilegio ad imprimendvw solvm
